PREFACE
   This code of the City of Wendell, as supplemented, contains ordinances up to
and including ordinance 561-2025, passed January 2, 2025. Ordinances of the
City adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the City
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
American Legal Publishing
Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not affect the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE NUMBER 297
   AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING THE CITY CODE OF WENDELL, IDAHO
    BE IT ORDAINED by the mayor and city council of the city of Wendell, Idaho,
an Idaho municipal corporation:
   Section 1: From and after the date of passage of this ordinance, the city
code of the city of Wendell, Idaho, prepared by Sterling Codifiers, Inc., under
the direction of the governing body of the city, containing all ordinances of a
general nature in effect at the time of such codification, shall be accepted in
all courts without question as the official code and law of the city as enacted
by the mayor and city council.
   Section 2: There is hereby adopted, as a method of perpetual codification,
the loose-leaf type of binding together with the continuous supplement service,
provided by Sterling Codifiers, Inc., whereby each newly adopted ordinance of a
general and permanent nature amending, altering, adding to or deleting
provisions of the official city code is identified by the proper catchline and
is inserted in the proper place in each of the official copies. Each such new
provision shall become effective upon the passage of the ordinance and the
insertion of the proper replacement pages in the copies of the code, three (3)
copies of which shall be maintained in the office of the city clerk, certified
as to correctness and available for inspection at any and all times that said
office is regularly open.
   Section 3: All ordinances of a general nature included in this official city
code shall be considered as a continuation of said ordinance provision and the
fact that some provisions have been deliberately eliminated by the governing
body shall not serve to cause any interruption in the continuous effectiveness
of ordinances included in said official city code. All ordinances of a special
nature, such as tax levy ordinances, bond ordinances, franchises, vacating
ordinances and annexation ordinances shall continue in full force and effect
unless specifically repealed or amended by a provision of the city code. Such
ordinances are not intended to be included in the official city code.
   Section 4: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to
change or amend by additions or deletions, any part or portion of such code, or
to insert or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such
code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the city to be
misrepresented thereby.
Any person, firm or corporation violating this section shall be punished as
provided in section 1-4-1 of the city code of Wendell, Idaho.
   Section 5: All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith are,
to the extent of such conflict, hereby repealed.
   Section 6: This ordinance and the code adopted by the same shall be in full
force and effect from and after its passage and approval in accordance with
law, as printed and published in book form by order of the mayor and city
council.
   PASSED BY THE COUNCIL and approved by the mayor of the city of Wendell,
Idaho this 26th day of January, 1978.

TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
WENDELL CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Code Alterations
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon adoption by the city council, this code is hereby declared to be and shall
hereafter constitute the official city code of the city of Wendell. This code
of ordinances shall be known and cited as the WENDELL MUNICIPAL CODE, and is
hereby published by authority of the city council and shall be kept up to date
as provided in section 1-1-3 of this chapter under the direction of the city
attorney, acting for the city council. Any reference to the number of any
section contained herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the
same number, its appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general
penalty clause relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when
reference is made to this code by title in any legal documents. (1977 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
The city code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in all administrative tribunals of this
state as the ordinances of the city of general and permanent effect, except the
excluded ordinances enumerated in section 1-2-1 of this title. (1977 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending the city code shall set forth the title, chapter and
section number of the section or sections to be amended, and this shall
constitute sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to
the amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the
codifiers and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in
its proper place in each copy of this code. Each such replacement page shall be
properly identified and shall be inserted in each individual copy of the city
code. (1977 Code)
1-1-4: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Replacement pages may
be inserted according to the official instructions when so authorized by the
city council. The city clerk shall see that the replacement pages are properly
inserted in the official copies maintained in the office of the city clerk. Any
person having in his custody an official copy of the city code shall make every
effort to maintain said code in an up to date and efficient manner. He shall
see to the immediate insertion of new or replacement pages when such are
delivered to him or made available to him through the office of the city clerk.
Said code books, while in actual possession of officials and other interested
persons, shall be and remain the property of the city and shall be returned to
the office of the city clerk when directed so to do by order of the city
council. (1977 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Court Proceedings
1-2-4: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the city passed prior to the adoption of this code
are hereby repealed, except such as are included in this code or are by
necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving
clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances; appropriation
ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations; franchise
ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places;
improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
city; and all special ordinances. (1977 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroad crossings with streets and other public ways,
or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities, shall
be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this code or by virtue of section 1-2-
1 of this chapter, excepting as this code may contain provisions for such
matters, in which case this code shall be considered as amending such ordinance
or ordinances in respect to such provisions only. (1977 Code)
1-2-3: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   (A)   No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former
ordinance whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as to any
offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done, any
penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or claim
arising under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any such
offense or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or
punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new
ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform
to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as
practicable, if any penalty, forfeiture or punishment be mitigated by any
provision of a new ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party
affected, applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes
effect.
   (B)   This section shall extend to all repeals, either by express words or
implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making any new provisions
upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   (C)   Nothing contained in this chapter shall be construed as abating any
action now pending under or by virtue of any general ordinance of the city
herein repealed, and the provisions of all general ordinances contained in this
code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions and not a new enactment of the
same provision; nor shall this chapter be deemed as discontinuing, abating,
modifying or altering any penalty accrued or to accrue, or as affecting the
liability of any person, firm or corporation, or as waiving any right of the
city under any ordinance or provision thereof in force at the time of the
adoption of this code. (1977 Code)
1-2-4: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase
of this code or any part thereof is for any reason held to be unconstitutional
or invalid or ineffective by any court of competent jurisdiction, such decision
shall not affect the validity or effectiveness of the remaining portions of
this code, or any part thereof. The city council hereby declares that it would
have passed each section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause
or phrase thereof irrespective of the fact that any one or more sections,
subsections, subdivisions, paragraphs, sentences, clauses or phrases be
declared unconstitutional, invalid or ineffective. (1977 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Construction Of Words
1-3-2: Definitions, General
1-3-3: Catchlines
1-3-1: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
   (A)   Whenever any word in any section of this code importing the plural
number is used in describing or referring to any matters, parties or persons,
any single matter, party or person shall be deemed to be included, although
distributive words may not have been used.
   (B)   When any subject matter, party or person is referred to in this code
by words importing the singular number only, or the masculine gender, several
matters, parties or persons and females as well as males and bodies corporate
shall be deemed to be included; provided, that these rules of construction
shall not be applied to any section of this code which contains any express
provision excluding such construction or where the subject matter or context
may be repugnant thereto.
   (C)   The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the city has been
changed in the content of this code to "title", "chapter", "section" and/or
"subsection", or words of like import, for organizational and clarification
purposes only. Such change to the city ordinances is not meant to amend passage
and effective dates of such original ordinances. (1977 Code)
1-3-2: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
Whenever the following words or terms are used in this code, they shall have
such meanings herein ascribed to them, unless the context makes such meaning
repugnant thereto:
AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another.
CITY: The city of Wendell, county of Gooding, state of Idaho.
EMPLOYEES: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city employee by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
Wendell".
FEE: A sum of money charged by the city for the carrying on of a business,
profession or occupation.
LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, profession
or occupation.
MISDEMEANOR: Any offense for which a sentence to a term of imprisonment in
other than a penitentiary for less than one year may be imposed.
NUISANCE: Anything offensive or obnoxious to the health and welfare of the
inhabitants of the city; or any act or thing repugnant to, or creating a hazard
to, or having a detrimental effect on the property of another person or to the
community.
OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this code or the omission of any
act required by the provisions of this code.
OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city officer by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
Wendell".
OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or profession.
OWNER: As applied to a building or land shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
PERSON: Any public or private corporation, firm, partnership, association,
organization, government or any other group acting as a unit, as well as a
natural person.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Includes every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and every right or
interest therein.
RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate
to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things in small quantities
direct to the consumer.
RIGHT OF WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
STREET: Includes alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
TENANT: As applied to a building or land shall include any person who occupies
the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with others.
WHOLESALER, WHOLESALE DEALER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be
understood to relate to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things in
quantity to persons who purchase for the purpose of resale.
WRITTEN, IN WRITING: May include printing and any other mode of representing
words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by
law to any official or public writing or bond required by law, it shall be in
the proper handwriting of such person, or in case he is unable to write, by his
proper mark. (1977 Code)
1-3-3: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of this code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
division or section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so
deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or
reenacted. (1977 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application
1-4-3: Liability Of Officers
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY:
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this code or ordinance of the
city, the penalty for which is not made an indictable misdemeanor by the laws
of the state of Idaho, shall be guilty of an offense, and shall, upon
conviction thereof or upon pleading guilty thereto, be punished by fine in an
amount not exceeding three hundred dollars ($300.00) for any one offense, or
shall be punished by imprisonment in the county jail for not more than six (6)
months, or by both such fine and imprisonment, recoverable with costs. (Ord.
320, 12-23-1980)
   (B)   The penalties set forth in this section shall supersede all penalties
for the violation of ordinances of the city heretofore enacted by the city
where applicable, and shall likewise govern and apply to all ordinances of the
city where no penalty is prescribed, and all future ordinances, unless a
different penalty be specifically prescribed. (Ord. 192, 11-10-1961)
1-4-2: APPLICATION:
   (A)   The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to every
section of this code the same as though it were a part of each and every
separate section. Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this
code where a duty is prescribed or obligation imposed, or where any action
which is of a continuing nature is forbidden or is declared to be unlawful,
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed upon each day such duty or obligation remains unperformed or such act
continues, unless otherwise specifically provided in this code.
   (B)   In all cases where the same offense is made punishable or is created
by different clauses or sections of this code, the prosecuting officer may
elect under which to proceed; but not more than one recovery shall be had
against the same person for the same offense; provided, that the revocation of
a license or permit shall not be considered a recovery or penalty so as to bar
any other penalty being enforced.
   (C)   Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to do any act
constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code and there shall
be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the provisions of
this chapter shall apply. (1977 Code)
1-4-3: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS:
No provision of this code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty, unless the intent of
the city council to impose such fine or penalty on such officer or employee is
specifically and clearly expressed in the section creating the duty. (1977
Code)
CHAPTER 5
MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-5-1: Meetings
1-5-2: Salaries
1-5-3: Fees Set By Resolution
1-5-1: MEETINGS:
   (A)   Day And Time: Regular meetings of the City Council shall be held on
the first and third Thursdays of each month, at the City Hall, at the hour of
six-thirty o’clock (6:30) P.M.
   (B)   Attendance:
      1.   The City Council hereby acknowledges that it is the duty of all
elected officials to attend all regular and special City Council meetings of
the City.
      2.   If an elected official is unable to attend a regular meeting, that
official shall notify the City Clerk, in writing or by email, acknowledged by
the City Clerk, at least one (1) week prior to the meeting date that he or she
will not be in attendance at the meeting. Failure to notify the City Clerk as
herein provided will result in a forfeiture of half of that elected official's
monthly salary for each meeting missed.
      3.   In no case shall an elected official be excused from more than four
(4) regular and/or special meetings in a calendar year. Any additional absences
will result in a forfeiture of one-half (½) of the elected official's monthly
salary.
      4.   In the event of an emergency that prohibits an elected official from
attending a meeting and/or providing the requisite notice, the elected official
is required to provide notice to the City Clerk as soon as reasonably possible.
Personal, medical, military service, work-related travel or weather-related are
hereby defined as emergency absences. Emergency absences do not count against
an elected official's four (4) permitted absences in a calendar year. (Ord.
436, 2-24-2004; amd. Ord. 531-2017, 6-15-2017, eff. 1-1-2018; Ord. 546-2-16-
2023)
1-5-2: SALARIES:
Commencing January 1, 2024, the salaries of the Mayor and members of the City
Council shall be as follows:
   (A)   Mayor: The Mayor shall receive a monthly salary in the sum of one
thousand two hundred dollars ($1,200.00);
   (B)   City Council: Each member of the City Council shall receive a monthly
salary in the sum of three hundred dollars ($300.00). (Ord. 452, 9-1-2005; amd.
Ord. 549-2023, 5-18-2023)
1-5-3: FEES SET BY RESOLUTION:
   (A)   All fees charged by the City shall be adopted by resolution rather
than by ordinance.
   (B)   A fee schedule shall be maintained at the Office of the City Clerk and
shall be available for inspection by the public, or for copying for a fee to be
determined by resolution as set by the City Council.
   (C)   In the event a fee is not provided by resolution, but is provided by
ordinance, the ordinance fee will still be applicable. In the event a fee is
set by both ordinance and resolution, the latest adopted fee shall apply. (Ord.
375, 5-11-1995)
CHAPTER 6
CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Appointment Of Officers; Terms
1-6-2: Salaries
1-6-3: Oath, Bond Of Officers
1-6-4: City Clerk
1-6-5: City Treasurer
1-6-6: Chief Of Police, Street Commissioner
1-6-7: City Engineer
1-6-8: Superintendent Of Waterworks
1-6-9: Standards And Training Of Police Officers
1-6-1: APPOINTMENT OF OFFICERS; TERMS:
The mayor shall, with the consent of the city council, appoint a city clerk,
city treasurer and city attorney, and such other officers, by resolution, as
may be deemed necessary for the efficient operation of the city, who shall hold
office until removed by the mayor for any cause by him deemed sufficient; but
such removal shall be by and with the affirmative vote of one-half (1/2) plus
one of the members of the full city council. In the alternative, these
appointed positions may be removed by a unanimous vote by all members of the
full city council on their own initiative. (Ord. 447, 4-7-2005)
1-6-2: SALARIES:
The salaries of all employees and all appointive officers of the city shall be
in such amounts as may be set by resolution of the city council from time to
time. (Ord. 204, 8-13-1965)
1-6-3: OATH, BOND OF OFFICERS:
Before entering upon the duties of their respective offices, each such
appointed city officer shall take and subscribe an oath to faithfully and
impartially perform the duties of his office; and shall execute a bond
conditioned on the faithful performance of his official duties, in such sum and
with securities to be approved by the city council. Said oath and bond of
officers shall be filed with the city clerk, with the exception of the oath and
bond of the city clerk, which shall be filed with the mayor. (Ord. 5, 12-3-
1909)
1-6-4: CITY CLERK:
The city clerk shall have the custody of all laws and ordinances of the city
and shall keep a correct journal of the proceedings of the city council. The
city clerk shall perform such other duties as are prescribed by the statutes of
the state or city ordinances. (Ord. 5, 12-3-1909)
1-6-5: CITY TREASURER:
The city treasurer shall be custodian of all money belonging to the city and
shall perform the duties prescribed by the statutes of the state or city
ordinances. (Ord. 5, 12-3-1909)
1-6-6: CHIEF OF POLICE, STREET COMMISSIONER:
   (A)   The offices of chief of police and street commissioner may be
combined. The duties of a street commissioner shall be as prescribed by the
city council.
   (B)   The chief of police shall keep such records and make such reports
concerning the activities of his department as may be required by statute or by
the mayor. He shall be responsible for the performance of the police department
and of its functions and all persons who are members of the police department
shall serve subject to his orders.
   (C)   It shall be the duty of the chief of police to see to the enforcement
of all provisions of this code and of all applicable statutes, and to preserve
order and prevent infractions of the law and arrest violators thereof. He shall
have authority to call upon any citizen or bystander to assist in the execution
of his duty. He shall serve all processes issued to him and enforce all orders
and judgments of the court. (1977 Code)
1-6-7: CITY ENGINEER:
It shall be the duty of the city engineer to set the grade for the laying of
all sidewalks, crossings and crosswalks, and to see that such are on the grade
established. The city engineer shall also do and perform all such other
services as are prescribed by statute of the state or city ordinance, or
required by the city council. (Ord. 5, 12-3-1909)
1-6-8: SUPERINTENDENT OF WATERWORKS:
There is hereby created in and for the city the office of superintendent of
waterworks. The superintendent shall, with the approval of the city council,
appoint such clerks and assistants and employ such labor as shall be necessary
for the operation of the waterworks system 1 . The superintendent shall have
charge of the maintenance and operation of said system, and all machinery,
property and appurtenances necessarily used in and about its operation and
maintenance; he shall direct the construction of all extensions to the system,
all connections and service pipes; he shall have full charge of and regulate
the water supply to all customers and to the fire hydrants; he shall read the
meters, render and collect all bills for service from the system; he shall
render a full and complete account of all the transactions of the waterworks
department once each month, or more often if required by the city council, such
report to be upon blanks to be provided by the city council. The superintendent
shall turn over to the city treasurer at least once a day all revenues of every
kind and nature derived from said waterworks system, and shall perform such
other duties in relation to the operation and maintenance of said system as the
city council may from time to time prescribe. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914; amd. 1977
Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 7, chapter 4 of this code.
1-6-9: STANDARDS AND TRAINING OF POLICE OFFICERS:
   (A)   The city hereby declares that it desires to qualify to receive aid for
police training from the law enforcement planning commission under the
provisions of title 19, chapter 51 and particularly section 19-5118 of the
Idaho Code.
   (B)   Pursuant to section 19-5117, Idaho Code, the city, while receiving aid
from the law enforcement planning commission pursuant to said chapter 51, will
adhere to the standards for employment and training established by the Idaho
peace officers standards and training advisory council. (Ord. 225, 5-14-1970)
CHAPTER 7
ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1-7-1: Election Precinct Established
1-7-2: Poll Hours
1-7-3: Election Procedures
1-7-1: ELECTION PRECINCT ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby established one election precinct for the city, which precinct
shall encompass and comprise all of the area of the city within the limits
thereof as now defined or as hereafter established, and which said precinct
shall be known as the precinct of Wendell. (Ord. 218, 9-11-1969)
1-7-2: POLL HOURS:
The polls shall be open on election day from eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. to eight
o'clock (8:00) P.M. in the city hall of Wendell, Idaho. (Ord. 471, 5-3-2007)
1-7-3: ELECTION PROCEDURES:
Election procedures are assigned to the county in accordance with state
statute. (Per correspondence dated 2-16-2012)
CHAPTER 8
CORPORATE SEAL
SECTION:
1-8-1: Corporate Seal
1-8-1: CORPORATE SEAL:
The corporate seal of the city shall be circular in form, with inner and outer
circles; it shall bear upon the space between the inner and outer circles the
words, "City of Wendell, Gooding County, Idaho", and upon the space within the
inner circle the words, "Incorporated October 12th, 1909", and in the center of
said space the word "SEAL". The seal described herein is hereby adopted as the
corporate seal of the city. (Ord. 2, 11-26-1909)
CHAPTER 9
OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER
SECTION:
1-9-1: Official Newspaper Designated
1-9-1: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER DESIGNATED:
The Twin Falls Times News is hereby appointed, designated and constituted the
official newspaper of the city of Wendell, Idaho. (Ord. 331, 12-8-1983; amd.
per correspondence dated 2-16-2012)
CHAPTER 10
INITIATIVE AND REFERENDUM
SECTION:
1-10-1: Creation Of Right
1-10-2: Number Of Petitioners Required
1-10-3: Time For Filing Petitions
1-10-4: Time For Election
1-10-5: Requirements For Signature, Verification Of Valid Petitions, Printing
Of Petition And Time Limits
1-10-1: CREATION OF RIGHT:
The people of this city shall have the right to enact ordinances through the
initiative process, and to repeal ordinances through the referendum process,
according to the procedures set forth herein. (Ord. 307, 3-22-1979)
1-10-2: NUMBER OF PETITIONERS REQUIRED:
To enact an ordinance by initiative or to repeal an ordinance by referendum,
there shall be attached or appended to the petition the signatures of the legal
voters of the city equal to at least twenty percent (20%) of the total number
of voters registered to vote at the last general election in the city. (Ord.
307, 3-22-1979)
1-10-3: TIME FOR FILING PETITIONS:
Referendum petitions with the requisite number of signatures attached shall be
filed with the city clerk not less than sixty (60) days following the final
adoption of the ordinance to be subject to referendum. (Ord. 307, 3-22-1979)
1-10-4: TIME FOR ELECTION:
A special election for initiative or referendum shall be provided not more than
ninety (90) days following the certification of the petition; provided, that in
the event a municipal election will occur within ninety (90) days, the
initiative or referendum shall be submitted at the time of the municipal
election. (Ord. 307, 3-22-1979)
1-10-5: REQUIREMENTS FOR SIGNATURE, VERIFICATION OF VALID PETITIONS, PRINTING
OF PETITION AND TIME LIMITS:
Referendum and initiative petitions shall conform with the requirements for
signature, verification of valid petitions, printing of petitions and time
limits, except as expressly modified to meet the purposes of initiative and
referendum to be as nearly as practicable as provided in sections 34-1701
through 34-1705 of the Idaho Code. (Ord. 307, 3-22-1979)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Commission Created
2-1-2: Membership; Appointment
2-1-3: Term Of Office
2-1-4: Vacancies
2-1-5: Removal
2-1-6: Political Affiliation; Compensation
2-1-7: Officers
2-1-8: Meetings; Quorum
2-1-9: Rules; Records; Open Meetings
2-1-10: Duties Generally
2-1-11: Cooperation
2-1-1: COMMISSION CREATED:
There is hereby created and established a commission to be known as the city
planning and zoning commission. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-2: MEMBERSHIP; APPOINTMENT:
The planning and zoning commission shall consist of seven (7) members to be
appointed by the mayor with the consent and approval of the city council. (Ord.
458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-3: TERM OF OFFICE:
The term of office for the first appointive members appointed to such
commission shall be two (2), four (4) and six (6) years, to be determined by
lot. Thereafter, the term of office for such appointed officer shall be six (6)
years. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-4: VACANCIES:
Vacancies occurring otherwise than throughout the expiration of terms, shall be
filled by the mayor and confirmed by the city council. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-5: REMOVAL:
Members may be removed by a majority vote of the body confirming the original
appointment. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-6: POLITICAL AFFILIATION; COMPENSATION:
Members shall be selected without respect to political affiliation. Members may
receive such mileage and per diem compensation not to exceed the current rate
established by the internal revenue service and the U.S. general services
administration per resolution 73 of the city. This mileage shall apply to the
attending of classes given specifically for planning and zoning information and
that the mayor has given his approval for the commission members to attend.
(Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-7: OFFICERS:
The commission shall select its own chairperson, and may create and fill such
other offices as it may determine necessary. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-8: MEETINGS; QUORUM:
The commission shall hold one regular meeting each month for not less than nine
(9) months of each year. A majority of the appointive members of the commission
shall be necessary to constitute a quorum at any meeting. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-9: RULES; RECORDS; OPEN MEETINGS:
Written rules consistent with the laws of the state shall be adopted for the
transaction of business and a written record of business, resolution, findings
and determinations shall be kept. All meetings and records shall be open to the
public. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-10: DUTIES GENERALLY:
It shall be the duty of the commission to recommend and make suggestions to the
city council for the adoption of the long range comprehensive plan for the
physical development of the city; for the formation of zoning districts; to
make suggestions concerning the laying out, widening, extending and locating of
streets, roads and highways for the relief of traffic; to make suggestions
concerning the density of population and development of land within the
jurisdiction of the city; to make suggestions concerning the future growth,
development and beautification of the city in respect to its public buildings,
streets, parks, grounds and lands consistent with the future growth and
development of the city in order to promote the public health, morals, safety
and welfare of the inhabitants thereof; and to do all such other things and
acts as may be provided by title 50, chapter 11, of the Idaho Code, and
amendments and additions thereto. (Ord. 458, 4-20-2006)
2-1-11: COOPERATION:
The commission may cooperate with other and like commissions for the purposes
as herein set forth and set forth in the statutes of the state. (Ord. 458, 4-
20-2006)
CHAPTER 2
BOARD OF PARK COMMISSIONERS
SECTION:
2-2-1: Board Created; Members
2-2-2: Terms Of Office
2-2-3: Organization
2-2-4: Vacancies
2-2-5: Duties
2-2-6: Gifts, Donations
2-2-7: Fund, Accounts
2-2-1: BOARD CREATED; MEMBERS:
There is hereby established and created a board to be known as the board of
park commissioners. The board shall consist of seven (7) members, who shall be
appointed by the mayor, with the consent of the city council, from residents of
the county of Gooding and one member of the city council who shall be an ex
officio member of the board. (Ord. 235, 7-23-1971)
2-2-2: TERMS OF OFFICE:
The terms of office of the respective members of the board of park
commissioners shall be as follows:
   (A)   The member appointed from the city council shall serve for a period of
two (2) years, or until the end of his period as a council member, whichever
occurs first.
   (B)   The remaining seven (7) members shall be appointed for a term of four
(4) years, except that those who are appointed as the initial board members
shall serve for a period as follows: Three (3) members shall be appointed for a
term of two (2) years; two (2) members for a term of three (3) years; and two
(2) members for a term of four (4) years. Thereafter, each appointment shall be
for a term of four (4) years. (Ord. 235, 7-23-1971)
2-2-3: ORGANIZATION:
The board of park commissioners shall meet on or before September 1 of each
year and appoint one of its members as chairperson, and one of its members as
vice chairperson, who may assume the duties of the chairperson in the event of
his absence, and shall also choose from its members a person who shall serve as
secretary of the board. These persons shall constitute the officers of the
board and shall retain their offices for a term of one year, or until their
successors have been selected. (Ord. 235, 7-23-1971; amd. 1977 Code)
2-2-4: VACANCIES:
All vacancies in the board of park commissioners, by reason of removal,
resignation or death, shall be filled by the mayor with the approval and
consent of the city council for the unexpired term of the person whose term was
so vacated. (Ord. 235, 7-23-1971)
2-2-5: DUTIES:
The board of park commissioners shall have the following duties:
   (A)   The planning and conduct of the recreation program of the city, the
recommending of personnel to conduct such program and the supervision of such
program.
   (B)   The operation, maintenance, control and supervision of parks and
swimming pools, and the power to establish rules and regulations, fixing rates
and charges and all other things as may be necessary to the maintenance and
operation of the parks and facilities located therein. (Ord. 235, 7-23-1971)
   (C)   The board shall submit to the mayor and city council, on or before the
first regular monthly meeting of September of each year, a recommended program
and a budget for the year, together with the board's recommendation as to the
personnel to be employed to operate, manage or supervise the program.
   (D)   The board, on or before the regular monthly meeting of September of
each year, shall submit to the mayor and city council a full and complete
report of recreation activities carried on by or under direction of the board.
(Ord. 235, 7-23-1971; amd. 1977 Code)
2-2-6: GIFTS, DONATIONS:
   (A)   Authority To Accept: The board of park commissioners shall have
authority on behalf of and in the name of the city, to accept gifts or
donations of property, both real and personal, grants of money from the federal
government, state of Idaho or monies from whatever source, and services useful
to the planning, construction and maintenance of the park system.
   (B)   Separate Fund: Monies received from grants, gifts or donations given
for purchase of lands and equipment for development of parks shall be kept in a
fund, separate from other city funds, and may be expended by the park board
upon prior approval of the city council. (Ord. 235, 7-23-1971)
2-2-7: FUND, ACCOUNTS:
The city clerk and city treasurer shall keep an account, to be designated as
the "park account", which account shall keep and show a proper account and
record of all property and money received, held or disbursed in the said fund;
provided, however, that the mayor and city council may from time to time
appoint a deputy clerk for the limited purpose of maintaining records and
accounts pertaining to the "park account", but that such deputy clerk shall not
be authorized to issue or execute warrants, or in any manner handle or control
any of the monies, property or funds of said account. (Ord. 244, 6-8-1972)
CHAPTER 3
GAS FITTERS EXAMINING BOARD
SECTION:
2-3-1: Board Established, Members
2-3-2: Qualifications Of Members
2-3-3: Duties And Powers
2-3-4: Application For Examination, Fee
2-3-5: Time Of Examination
2-3-6: Reexamination
2-3-7: Certificate Of Competency
2-3-8: Revocation Of Certificate
2-3-9: Compensation Of Board Members
2-3-1: BOARD ESTABLISHED, MEMBERS:
A board to be known as the gas fitters examining board shall be appointed by
the mayor with the advice and consent of the city council. It shall consist of
three (3) members selected from nominees recommended by an organized and
generally recognized association of responsible firms or individuals engaged in
the gas fitting or related pipe fitting industry, and who shall qualify as
hereinafter prescribed. The members of the first board shall be appointed
within sixty (60) days after the effective date hereof and shall serve for the
following terms: one member for one year; one member for two (2) years; and one
member for three (3) years. Thereafter, upon the expiration of each term, the
board members shall be appointed for a term of three (3) years. All board
members shall be subject to removal by the mayor, with the advice and consent
of the city council, for malfeasance in office, neglect of duty or incapacity
to serve. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957; amd. 1977 Code)
2-3-2: QUALIFICATIONS OF MEMBERS:
All members of the gas fitters examining board shall be United States citizens,
residents of the state of Idaho for not less than one year, engaged in a
responsible capacity in the gas fitting business prior to appointment and
during the term of office and qualified by integrity, knowledge and experience
to judge the competency of applicants for gas fitters certificates. Not less
than one member of the board shall have had five (5) years' or more experience
as a gas fitting contractor, gas fitting journeyman or as an engineer
experienced in the design, construction and operation of gas systems. (Ord.
172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-3: DUTIES AND POWERS:
The gas fitters examining board shall conduct examinations for the purpose of
determining the competency of applicants who are required to have a license
under this chapter and chapter 7, title 3 of this code, and to issue
certificates of competency to such persons as may be entitled thereto. The
board shall elect a chairperson from its members, who shall be the executive
officer and preside at all meetings, and a secretary, who shall keep such
records as are proper for efficient discharge of the board's duties, which
records pertaining to an applicant's qualifications shall be kept intact and
available in the event of dispute for a period of not less than one year
following the date of issuance of the certificate of competency. The board
shall determine the character and extent of the examination based on the
requirements of this code, and shall grade and pass or reject the applicant on
the basis of equaling or exceeding, or failing to equal, a minimum percentage
grade of seventy percent (70%). The board shall issue certificates of
competency to successful applicants and shall have the power to revoke such
certificates under conditions hereinafter prescribed. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-4: APPLICATION FOR EXAMINATION, FEE:
   (A)   Form Of Application: Any person required by this chapter or chapter 7,
title 3 of this code to be licensed shall make application on the form provided
to the city clerk, acting for the gas fitters examining board, for the
examination for a certificate of competency and pay the examination fee. (Ord.
172, 1-9-1957)
   (B)   Fee Set By Resolution: The applicant shall pay to the city clerk at
the time of making application an examination fee as set by resolution pursuant
to section
1-5-3 of this code. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957; amd. Ord. 375, 5-11-1995)
   (C)   Registration For Apprentice Gas Fitters: Apprentice gas fitters shall
not be required to be examined but shall be registered with the board and shall
maintain their certificate cards showing classification. The board shall notify
the city clerk of this registration.
   (D)   Placement In General Fund: All monies derived from the payment of
examination fees shall be placed in the general fund. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-5: TIME OF EXAMINATION:
The gas fitters examining board shall so schedule its meetings to examine a
single applicant, or as many applicants at one time as circumstances dictate,
but in no case shall an applicant be required to delay his examination more
than sixty (60) days from the date the application is accepted. Each applicant
shall be notified by the board of the time and place for examination not less
than forty eight (48) hours prior to examination time. Notification by
registered letter directed to the address given on the application shall be
considered notification. Failure of the applicant to appear for examination
does not entitle him to a refund of the examination fee. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-6: REEXAMINATION:
Any person who, for sufficient cause in the judgment of the gas fitters
examining board, was unable to appear for examination at the stated time, may
apply and be given an examination after thirty (30) days for the original fee
payment. Any person who fails to pass the examination may apply for
reexamination after a period of thirty (30) days upon payment of the
examination fee. Should any person fail to pass the examination the second
time, the board may refuse the application until the expiration of six (6)
months. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-7: CERTIFICATE OF COMPETENCY:
Upon successful completion of an examination, the gas fitters examining board
shall issue to the applicant a certificate of competency in the form of a card,
providing thereon the applicant's name, classification, year in which current,
space for the applicant's signature and license number, and the signature of
the chairperson of the board of examiners. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-8: REVOCATION OF CERTIFICATE:
A certificate of competency may be revoked by the gas fitters examining board
if it has good and sufficient evidence that such certificate was obtained by
fraud, or if the holder demonstrates lack of knowledge or incompetency in
matters relevant to such certificate. In such cases the board may order
reexamination, or may refuse application for reexamination as conditions may
dictate. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
2-3-9: COMPENSATION OF BOARD MEMBERS:
The members of the gas fitters examining board shall each receive from the city
as the only compensation for their services the sum of five dollars ($5.00) for
each journeyman fitter examined. (Ord. 172, 1-9-1957)
CHAPTER 4
TREE BOARD 1
SECTION:
2-4-1: Board Established
2-4-2: Duties And Authority
2-4-3: Meetings
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 7, chapter 7 of this code.
2-4-1: BOARD ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby created and established a city tree board, which shall consist
of five (5) members, citizens and residents of the city, who shall be appointed
by the mayor with the approval of the city council. Members of the board shall
serve without compensation. In the event that a vacancy shall occur, this
position will be filled by an appointment by the mayor with the approval of the
city council. (Ord. 434, 11-18-2003)
2-4-2: DUTIES AND AUTHORITY:
   (A)   Duties: Duties of the tree board shall include, but are not limited
to, the following:
      1.   Provide advice to the mayor and city council as to appropriate
practices for the preservation and management of trees.
      2.   Have an inventory taken of all existing trees on all city
properties.
      3.   Provide information to the public on the care and planting of trees.
      4.   Assist in Arbor Day celebrations and activities.
      5.   Identify and implement suitable landscaping projects for city
property.
      6.   Plan and review, with the city council, a forest program budget.
   (B)   Authority: The mayor and city council have ultimate authority over all
trees on or within the city properties and the tree board's authority is only
to give recommendations to the mayor and city council. (Ord. 434, 11-18-2003)
2-4-3: MEETINGS:
Meetings of the board shall be held when duly called by the chairperson by
written or oral notice. A majority of the members of the board shall be
necessary to form a quorum at any meeting. All meetings shall be open to the
public. A written record of meetings shall be kept, which record shall be made
public. Any meeting of the board may also be called by the mayor. (Ord. 434,
11-18-2003)
TITLE 3
BUSINESS REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUSINESS LICENSING
SECTION:
3-1-1: Applicability
3-1-2: License Required
3-1-3: Exemptions
3-1-4: Business License Application
3-1-5: Additional Requirements For Mobile Food Businesses
3-1-6: Additional Requirements For Ice Cream Truck Businesses
3-1-7: Business License Denial, Suspension, Revocation; Hearing; Appeal;
Penalties
3-1-1: APPLICABILITY:
The provisions of this chapter shall be applicable to all businesses. A
"business" is defined as any wholesale and retail businesses and all
activities, occupational callings, trades, pursuits or professions that conduct
business from a location within the City of Wendell with the object of gain,
profit, benefit or advantage. Each business location shall be deemed a separate
business unless it is a specific annex to the main location of the business.
This chapter is not intended to repeal any license or franchise provisions of
any other ordinance of the City of Wendell, nor is the license issued pursuant
to this chapter to be considered a waiver of any other requirements of
compliance with any federal, state or local laws. (Ord. 559-2024, 10-17-2024)
3-1-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall engage in any business within the City of Wendell for which
licensing is required by this chapter, without having submitted a business
license application (as hereinafter defined) to the City Clerk and receiving a
license from the City of Wendell to operate the business ("business license")
in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. The business license shall
be in addition to any other requirements of this chapter or the other
provisions of this chapter. A business license shall be valid for the remainder
of the calendar year in which it is granted so long as the ownership,
management, nature of the business or location of business remains unchanged or
is not otherwise suspended or revoked as provided for herein. (Ord. 559-2024,
10-17-2024)
3-1-3: EXEMPTIONS:
   A.   The fee provisions of this chapter shall not apply to:
      1.   Persons participating in charitable activities within the meaning of
Section 501(C)(3) of the United States Internal Revenue Code. Possession of a
certificate of such status from the Internal Revenue Service shall be required
to qualify for this exemption.
      2.   Any agency of the United States Government and any political sub-
division of the State of Idaho.
      3.   Persons who occupy space at a flea market, including the operator of
the flea market.
      4.   Persons who make occasional sales of their own household property
not more than twice each calendar year.
      5.   Domestic servants, newspaper carriers or casual labor not including
temporary employees of a regularly conducted business.
      6.   Landlords of any residential property having one (1) or two (2)
family units. (Ord. 559-2024, 10-17-2024)
3-1-4: LICENSE APPLICATION:
   A.   To obtain a business license, the applicant ("applicant") must submit
an application ("business license application") to the City Clerk.
   B.   Business license applications can be obtained from the City Clerk's
Office or found on the City of Wendell website.
   C.   Business license application shall include such information as may be
required by the City Council including, but not limited to:
      1.   Name (Owner and Manager).
      2.   Applicant Address (Owner and Manager).
      3.   Applicant phone number (Owner and Manager).
      4.   Physical and mailing address and phone number of the business.
      5.   Nature of the business being conducted.
   D.   Every business license application shall be accompanied by a fee as may
be established by the City Council from time to time ("business license fee").
   E.   Every business license application shall be signed by the owner of the
business or his agent and submitted to the City Clerk's Office within ten (10)
business days of the opening of the business.
   F.   Any changes in the business as directed in Section
3-1-4(C) shall be submitted to the City Clerk's Office within ten (10) business
days of the changes.
   G.   Irrespective of the date of the business license application, the
initial business license shall be valid from the date of the approval of the
business license until the end of the calendar year.
   H.   The business license fee shall be set by resolution of the City Council
and must be paid at the time the business license application is submitted to
the City Clerk's Office and prior to the issuance of a business license. City
services, where applicable, will not be turned on until the business license is
approved.
   I.   Every business required under this chapter to obtain a business license
shall display such license in a prominent location upon the business premises.
No business shall loan, sell, give, or assign to any other person or allow any
other person to use or display, destroy, damage or remove a business license,
or to have in his possession any business license which was not issued to that
business.
   J.   Whenever the ownership of a business, nature of the business or
location of any business within the City of Wendell is changed, a new business
license application reflecting the change shall be presented to the Clerk's
Office within ten (10) business days of said change. The issuance of the new
business license shall be valid until the end of the calendar year in which it
was issued.
   K.   Whenever the management of the Business changes, the Clerk's Office
shall be notified in writing of the new manager's name, address and phone
number within ten (10 ) business days of said change.
   L.   The holder of a Business License ("business licensee") shall comply
with all applicable federal, state and local laws and regulations.
   M.   A business license may be denied, suspended, or revoked for failure of
the business licensee to comply with the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 559-
2024, 10-17-2024)
3-1-5: LICENSE FEE:
   A.   In addition to the requirements for a business license, a mobile food
businesses which is defined as a business that serves food or beverages from a
self-contained unit or in a trailer with wheels and conducts all or part of its
operations on premises other than its own shall provide annually to the City of
Wendell at the beginning of each year:
      1.   Written permission from the property owner to allow the operation of
a mobile food business.
      2.   Confirmation of permission from the property owner allowing
employees and customers access to a commercially plumbed public restroom on
site.
      3.   Provide site plan depicting the location of the mobile food business
on the property in compliance with the restrictions listed herein. A site plan
must be provided for each location to be utilized by the mobile food business.
      4.   Temporary connections to potable water are prohibited. Water must be
supplied from an internal tank attached to the mobile food business.
      5.   Electricity shall be from a generator or an electrical outlet that
is in compliance with the electrical code enforced by the State of Idaho,
Electrical Bureau, Division of Public Safety.
      6.   A copy of the electrical permit issued by the State of Idaho must be
presented to the City of Wendell prior to a business license for a mobile food
business being issued.
      7.   Applicant must provide a copy of the plan for the removal of gras
water from the Mobile Food Business location. Connection to the City of Wendell
sewer system is prohibited. The plan for removal of the gray water from the
location must be approved by the City of Wendell Public Works Administrator.
      8.   A fire inspection must be completed by the City of Wendell Fire
Department prior to a Business License for a mobile food business being issued.
Fire inspections must be completed annually for licensing. The mobile food
business must meet and maintain all current Fire Code requirements.
      9.   Applicant must provide a copy of the health permit issued by the
South-Central Health District annually.
      10.   Applicant must provide a State of Idaho Tax Identification Number
annually.
      11.   Applicant must provide current proof of public liability insurance
in an amount not to exceed the single-limit coverage of at least five hundred
thousand dollars ($500.000.00) for the mobile food business.
      12.   Mobile food businesses must provide a garbage container capable of
holding all trash and garbage generated by the operation of said business. The
container must be emptied periodically as necessary. The immediate areas
surrounding the mobile food business must be kept free of litter, grease and
other debris at all times.
      13.   A drive through is not permitted in conjunction with any mobile
food business.
      14.   All signage must be securely attached to the mobile food business
unit.
      15.   Only canopies which are part of the mobile food business itself and
supported only by the mobile food business unit will be allowed.
   B.   A Mobile Food Business:
      1.   Shall be located on private property in commercially zoned areas
where an existing, permanent business operates in a building with a certificate
of occupancy.
      2.   Are not allowed on any City of Wendell properly or right-of-way
unless invited by an event sponsor through the special event application
process.
      3.   Shall not be located in the following areas:
         (a)   Within six (6) feet from the edge of any public sidewalk,
driveway, utility box, vaults, handicap ramps, or emergency call boxes.
         (b)   Within ten (10) feet of any doorway, building entrance/exit, or
other building structure.
         (c)   Within fifteen (15) feet of a fire hydrant.
         (d)   In any area that obstructs the movement/visibilily of vehicles
or bicycles using the appropriate public right-of-way, access easements, drive
aisle, or interferes with pedestrian use of the same.
         (e)   Likewise, no associated outdoor seating, or other items related
to the mobile food business shall violate the restrictions above.
      4.   Mobile food businesses shall not use or attach any items to public
amenities (trees, streetlights, street furniture, railing, etc.) for any
reason.
   C.   A mobile food businesses which is readily movable without disassembling
for transport to another location shall provide annual proof of mobility by
physically driving the mobile food business to city hall for a physical
inspection bv the City Clerk, or their designee, at a scheduled time designated
by the City Clerk. (Ord. 559-2024, 10-17-2024)
3-1-6: DISPLAY OF LICENSE:
In addition to the requirements for a business license, the owner of an ice
cream truck, which is defined as any motor vehicle used for selling, displaying
or offering to sell any frozen dairy product or frozen water-based food product
including, but not limited to, ice cream, popsicles, ice sherbert. frozen
desserts and as incidental thereto other food items which are prepackaged by
the manufacturer such as gum, candy, juice, chips and soft drinks or similar
products that do not require further processing, shall:
   A.   Conspicuously display its business license which shall be clearly
visible on the windshield of any ice cream truck operated within City of
Wendell limits.
   B.   Provide a current/valid driver's license for each individual operating
the ice cream truck.
   C.   Provide a copy of current proof of liability insurance. Each applicant
for a business license or renewal under this section shall submit with its
application a certificate of insurance executed by an insurance company or
association authorized to transact business in The State of Idaho, that there
is in effect liability insurance in an amount not less than five hundred
thousand dollars ($500,000.00) combined single limits for both general
liability and business liability coverage. Such policy or policies shall
include coverage of all motor vehicles used in connection with applicant's
business. The certificate shall contain a statement that the City of Wendell
will be given written notification at least thirty (30) days prior to
cancellation or material change in the coverage. Cancellation shall constitute
grounds for revocation of the business license issued hereunder unless another
insurance policy complying herewith is provided and is in effect at the time of
cancellation/termination.
   D.   Applicant shall provide a copy of the health permit issued by the
South-Central Health District annually.
   E.   An ice cream truck may only operate one half (½) hour after sunrise to
one half (½) hour before sunset.
   F.   An ice cream truck may operate on any public streets within the City of
Wendell limits subject to the following limitations and requirements:
      1.   An ice cream truck shall have a clearly audible backup warning
device that activates whenever the vehicle is shifted into reverse gear.
      2.   An ice cream truck shall have at least two (2) flashing yellow
beacons on the roof of the vehicle, one (1) at the front and one (1) at the
rear. One (1) roof mounted light must be visible from all sides of the vehicle.
These beacons shall be activated whenever merchandise is being sold, offered
for sale, or displayed for sale.
      3.   An ice cream truck shall have a sign or decal on the front and on
the rear of the vehicle, in letters at least six (6) inches in height and
visible for two hundred (200) feet along a level, straight road way,
identifying the vehicle as an ice cream truck and containing the words
"Children Crossing".
      4.   The operator of an ice cream truck shall be prohibited from pulling
a trailer.
      5.   The operator of an ice cream truck may not sell, offer to sell, or
display for sale its merchandise on public streets where the speed limit
exceeds twenty-five (25) miles per hour.
      6.   The operator of an ice cream truck may not sell, offer to sell, or
display for sale its merchandise to any person standing in the roadway.
      7.   The operator of an ice cream truck may not operate in reverse in
order to sell, offer to sell, or display for sale its merchandise.
      8.   The operator of an ice cream truck may not sell, offer to sell, or
display for sale any of its merchandise at any stop sign or within thirty (30)
feet of a roadway intersection.
      9.   The operator of an ice cream truck shall pull as far off the roadway
as possible to sell, offer to sell, or display for sale its merchandise and do
so only from the side of the Ice Cream Truck away from moving traffic and as
near as possible to the curb or side of the street. (Ord. 559-2024, 10-17-2024)
3-1-7: CHANGE OF OWNERSHIP, MANAGEMENT, NATURE OF BUSINESS OR LOCATION OF
BUSINESS:
   A.   If the City Clerk determines that facts exist for denial, suspension,
or revocation of a business license under this chapter, the City Clerk shall
notify the applicant or business licensee (respondent ) in writing of the
intent to deny, suspend or revoke the business license. including the grounds
therefor, by personal delivery, or by certified mail. The notification shall be
directed to the most current business address on file with the City Clerk.
Within five (5) working days of receipt of such notice, the respondent may
provide to the Mayor and City Council in writing a response that shall include
a statement of reasons why the business license or permit should not be denied,
suspended, or revoked. Within five (5) days of the receipt of respondent's
written response, the Mayor shall notify respondent in writing of the hearing
date on respondent's denial, suspension. or revocation proceeding.
   B.   Within ten (10) working days of the receipt of respondent's written
response, the Mayor and City Council shall conduct a hearing at which
respondent shall have the opportunity to be represented by counsel and present
evidence and witnesses on his or her behalf. If a response is not received by
the Major and City Council in the time stated or if after the hearing the City
Council finds that grounds as specified in this chapter exist for denial,
suspension, or revocation, then such denial, suspension, or revocation shall
become final five (5) days after the Mayor sends, by certified mail, written
notice that the business license has been denied, suspended, or revoked. Such
notice shall include a statement advising the applicant or business licensee of
the right to appeal such decision to a court of competent jurisdiction.
   C.   If the City Council finds that no grounds exist for denial, suspension,
or revocation of a business license then within five (5) days after the
hearing, the Mayor shall withdraw the intent to deny, suspend, or revoke the
business license and shall so notify the respondent in writing by certified
mail of such action and shall contemporaneously therewith issue the business
license.
   D.   When a decision to deny, suspend or revoke a business license becomes
final the applicant or business licensee (aggrieved party) whose application
for a business license has been denied or whose business license has been
suspended or revoked shall have the right to appeal such action to a court of
competent jurisdiction as allowed by law. Upon the filing of any court action
to appeal, challenge, restrain or otherwise enjoin the City of Wendell's
enforcement of the denial, suspension or revocation, the City of Wendell shall
immediately issue the aggrieved party a provisional business license. The
provisional business license shall allow the aggrieved party to continue
operation of the business licensee's business and will expire upon the court's
entry of a judgment on the aggrieved party's action to appeal challenge
restrain or otherwise enjoin the City of Wendell's enforcement.
   E.   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
deemed guilty of an infraction and shall be assessed a fixed penalty of one
hundred dollars ($100.00) excluding court costs and fees. A second and any
subsequent conviction for a violation of the provisions of this chapter within
five (5) years shall constitute a misdemeanor, punishable by imprisonment in a
county jail not exceeding six (6) months, or by a fine not exceeding one
thousand dollars ($1.000.00), or by both. Each day such violation is committed,
or permitted to continue, shall constitute a separate offense and shall be
punishable as such hereunder.
F.   Instead of, or in addition to the penalties or relief provided above the
City of Wendell may take such other available legal action as is necessary to
prevent or remedy any violation of this chapter. A civil action may be
commenced and pursued in the Gooding County Court for the purpose of enforcing
or correcting any violation of this chapter, including but not limited to an
order enjoining or preventing operation of the business in violation of this
chapter. (Ord. 559-2024, 10-17-2024)
CHAPTER 2
CARD, AMUSEMENT TABLES
(Rep. by Ord. 453, 12-5-2005)
CHAPTER 3
BEER REGULATIONS
SECTION:
3-3-1: Purpose
3-3-2: Definitions
3-3-3: License Required, Term, Fees
3-3-4: Application For License
3-3-5: Premises Requirements
3-3-6: Police Right Of Inspection
3-3-7: Sales Restrictions
3-3-8: Revocation Of License
3-3-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter shall be deemed an exercise of the police powers of the city for
the protection of the public health, peace and morals, and all of its
provisions shall be liberally construed for the attainment of that purpose.
(Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
3-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms as used in this chapter are hereby defined as follows:
BEER: Any beverage obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion or
decoction of barley, malt and/or other ingredients in drinkable water.
RETAILER: Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of beer to the
consumer. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935; amd. 1977 Code)
3-3-3: LICENSE REQUIRED, TERM, FEES:
It shall be unlawful for any retailer to sell, trade, barter or dispose of beer
within the city without first having obtained a license therefor from the city
council as hereinafter provided. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
   (A)   All licenses issued under this chapter shall terminate at twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight on December 31 of each year. (Ord. 318, 11-13-1980)
   (B)   Retailer's license fee for the sale only of bottled and canned beer,
none of which is consumed on the premises where sold, shall be as set by
resolution pursuant to section
1-5-3 of this code, and where such bottled or canned beer is consumed on the
premises where sold, the license fee shall be as set by resolution pursuant to
section
1-5-3 of this code. If the license is granted between January 1 and July 1, the
applicant must pay the full annual license fee. If the license is granted
between July 1 and December 31, the applicant must pay one-half (1/2) of the
annual license fee.
   (C)   Retailer's license fee for the sale of draught and bottled or canned
beer, or draught beer only, shall be as set by resolution pursuant to section
1-5-3 of this code. If the license is granted between January 1 and July 1, the
applicant must pay the full annual license fee. If the license is granted
between July 1 and December 31, the applicant must pay one-half (1/2) of the
annual license fee. (Ord. 142, 9-29-1947; amd. Ord. 375, 5-11-1995)
3-3-4: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Every retailer desiring to obtain a license for the sale, barter, trade or
distribution of beer shall make a written application therefor to the city
council, which said application shall contain the following information:
   (A)   Name and residence of applicant.
   (B)   Legal description of room or building in which said business shall be
conducted.
   (C)   That applicant is a citizen of the United States and has been a bona
fide resident of the state of Idaho for a period of one year prior to the date
of making application. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
   (D)   That applicant is of good moral character and is over the age of
nineteen (19) years. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935; amd. 1977 Code)
   (E)   That applicant has not been convicted of any felony or of the
violation of any law regulating, governing or prohibiting the sale of alcoholic
beverages or intoxicating liquor. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
3-3-5: PREMISES REQUIREMENTS:
Retailers' licenses shall be granted only for a certain room or building
designated in said license, which said room or building shall be well lighted
and the view thereof not obstructed by any curtain, blind or partition, and the
place of business shall not be changed or moved without the consent of the city
council in regular session. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
3-3-6: POLICE RIGHT OF INSPECTION:
Every person to whom a license shall be granted to sell, barter, trade or
dispose of beer shall at all times conduct a quiet and orderly place of
business which shall be open to the inspection at all times of any police
officer, or officer of the United States; and the persons or either or any of
them shall have the right at any and all times to make an examination of the
licensed premises to ascertain if the licensee of such premises is conforming
to the provisions of this chapter, the laws of the state, or the laws of the
United States applicable thereto, and to check the alcoholic content of any
beer or other beverages being kept so posted during the full period for which
said license is issued, and the license shall not be sold, transferred or
assigned without the consent of the city council. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
3-3-7: SALES RESTRICTIONS:
No beer shall be sold, traded, bartered or disposed of in the city, save and
except within the fire limits of the city, or sold, traded, bartered or
disposed of within three hundred feet (300') of any public school grounds or
church in the city, except with the approval of the governing body of the
municipality after any public school or church located within three hundred
feet (300') of such location is provided written notice and an opportunity to
comment; provided that this limitation shall not apply to any duly licensed
premises that at the time of licensing did not come within the restricted area
but subsequent to licensing came therein.
The days and hours for the sale of beer shall be the same as those set by the
commission of Gooding County, state of Idaho. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935; amd. 1977
Code; Ord. 495-A, 12-4-2008; Ord. 539-2021, 7-6-2021)
3-3-8: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The right shall be and at all times remain vested in the city council to revoke
or cancel the license of any person licensed hereunder for any violation of
this chapter, and upon complaint filed with the mayor, the mayor shall notify
the offender to appear before the city council and be heard upon said
complaint, and if at the hearing it shall appear to the city council that cause
exists for the cancellation or revocation of said license, then such license
shall be revoked without further process of law. (Ord. 116, 6-14-1935)
CHAPTER 4
LIQUOR BY THE DRINK
SECTION:
3-4-1: Definitions
3-4-2: License Required, Fee
3-4-3: Application For License
3-4-4: Investigation Of Application
3-4-5: Form Of License, Expiration
3-4-6: Persons Not Qualified For Licensing
3-4-7: Sanitary Requirements
3-4-8: Location Restrictions
3-4-9: Police Right To Examine Premises
3-4-10: Hours Of Sale
3-4-11: Restriction Of Sales By Licensee
3-4-12: Purchase By Unqualified Persons
3-4-13: Revocation And Cancellation Of License
3-4-14: Penalty
3-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the definitions contained in section 23-902 of
the Idaho Code are, by this reference, incorporated herein and made section
3-4-1 of this chapter. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-2: LICENSE REQUIRED, FEE:
The city council, at a regular or special meeting, shall issue licenses to
qualified applicants, as herein provided, and upon the issuance of such
license, the licensee therein named shall be authorized to sell liquor at
retail by the drink, but only in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
Each licensee licensed under the provisions of this chapter shall pay an annual
licensee fee to the city in an amount as set by resolution pursuant to section
1-5-3 of this code. (Ord. 248, 12-14-1972; amd. Ord. 375, 5-11-1995)
3-4-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Each applicant for license shall file with the city clerk an application
verified by affidavit, setting forth the following facts:
   (A)   Description of premises for which license is sought and its location,
and name of owner of said premises.
   (B)   The names and addresses of all persons who will have any financial
interest in any business to be carried on in and upon the licensed premises,
whether such interest results from open loans, mortgages, conditional sales
contracts, silent partnerships, trusts or any other basis than open trade
accounts, incurred in the ordinary course of business, and the amounts of such
interests.
   (C)   If premises to be licensed is not owned by the applicant, then a
certified copy of the lease by which he will occupy the premises showing that
the owner consents to the sale of liquor by the drink on such premises.
   (D)   The name and address of the applicant, which shall include all members
of a partnership or association and the officers and members of the governing
board and ten (10) principal stockholders of a corporation.
   (E)   A copy of the articles of incorporation and bylaws of any corporation,
the articles of association and bylaws of any association, or the articles of
partnership of any partnership.
   (F)   If during the period of any license issued hereunder, any change shall
take place in any of the requirements of subsection (A), (B), (C), (D) or (E)
of this section, the licensee shall forthwith make a verified report of such
change to the city clerk. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-4: INVESTIGATION OF APPLICATION:
Upon receipt of an application for a license under this chapter, accompanied by
the necessary license fee, the city council may make such investigation of all
matters pertaining thereto as they shall deem proper. If the city council shall
determine the contents of the application are true, that such applicant is
qualified to receive a license, that his premises is suitable for the carrying
on of the business and requirements of this chapter are met and complied with,
the license shall be issued, otherwise the application shall be denied and the
license fee returned. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-5: FORM OF LICENSE, EXPIRATION:
Every license issued under this chapter shall set forth the name of the person
to whom issued, the location by street and number, or other definite
designation, of the premises. If issued to a partnership, names of the persons
constituting the partnership shall be set forth; if issued to a corporation or
association, the names of the principal officers and the governing board shall
be set forth. Such license shall be signed by the licensee and shall be
nontransferable. Every license issued under the provisions of this chapter is
separate and distinct and no person except the licensee therein named shall
exercise any of the privileges granted thereunder, and all licenses are
applicable only to premises in respect to which issued. All licenses shall
expire at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on December 31 of the calendar year
for which issued. No person shall be granted more than one license in any one
year. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-6: PERSONS NOT QUALIFIED FOR LICENSING:
The provisions of section 23-910 of the Idaho Code are by this reference
incorporated herein and made section
3-4-6 of this chapter, and this further provision is added: A license shall not
be issued to a person not of good moral character. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-7: SANITARY REQUIREMENTS:
Any licensed premises shall be maintained in sanitary condition according to
the requirements of chapter 16, title 39 of the Idaho Code. (Ord. 140, 6-24-
1947)
3-4-8: LOCATION RESTRICTIONS:
No license shall be issued for any premises in any neighborhood which is
predominantly residential or within three hundred feet (300') of any public
school, church or any other place of worship, measured in a straight line to
the nearest entrance of the licensed premises; provided, that this limitation
shall not apply to any duly licensed premises that at the time of licensing did
not come within the restricted area but subsequent to licensing became therein.
(Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-9: POLICE RIGHT TO EXAMINE PREMISES:
Any duly authorized police officer of the city shall have the right at any time
to make an examination of the premises of any licensee as to whether the laws
of the state and the ordinances of the city are being complied with. (Ord. 140,
6-24-1947)
3-4-10: HOURS OF SALE:
The days and hours for the sale of liquor shall be the same as those set by the
commission of Gooding County, state of Idaho. (Ord. 495-A, 12-4-2008)
3-4-11: RESTRICTION OF SALES BY LICENSEE:
No licensee or his employed agents, servants or bartenders shall sell, deliver
or give away, or cause or permit to be sold, delivered or given away any liquor
to: (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
   (A)   Any person under the age of nineteen (19) years. (Ord. 245, 6-22-1972)
   (B)   Any person actually, apparently or obviously intoxicated.
   (C)   A habitual drunkard.
   (D)   An interdicted person. (Ord. 140, 6-24-1947)
3-4-12: PURCHASE BY UNQUALIFIED PERSONS:
Any person under the age of nineteen (19) years, or other person who knowingly
misrepresents his qualifications for the purpose of obtaining liquor from such
licensee, shall be equally guilty with such licensee and shall, upon conviction
thereof, be guilty of an offense. (Ord. 245, 6-22-1972)
3-4-13: REVOCATION AND CANCELLATION OF LICENSE:
The right shall be and at all times remain vested in the city council to revoke
or cancel the license of any person licensed hereunder for any violation of
this chapter; and upon verified complaint filed with the city council, the city
council shall cause such alleged offender to appear before the city council and
be heard upon said complaint. A copy of said complaint shall be served with
said notice, and the day and hour of the hearing, which shall be at least five
