monument shall be at least twenty four inches (24") in vertical height. The
iron rod shall be a minimum of twenty four inches (24") long, extending one
inch (1") above the top of the concrete monument. The top of the monument shall
set flush in the finished roadway surface. Block corners and boundary corners
shall be five-eighths inch (5/8") diameter iron rod, at least thirty inches
(30") in length. Lot corners shall be one-half inch (1/2") diameter steel rods
at least twenty four inches (24") in length.
   (L)   Closed Traverse Computation: A copy of the closed traverse
computations which shall be sufficiently complete to show that all boundaries
of lots, blocks and the entire subdivision close to an accuracy of not less
than one part in four thousand (4,000). (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
6-3-4: PROCEDURE FOR FILING:
   (A)   Submission: The final plat shall be submitted to the city clerk, who
shall forward it to the planning and zoning commission for approval. Expenses
shall be paid by the subdivider.
   (B)   Planning And Zoning Commission Approval: The planning and zoning
commission shall check the final plat with the conditionally approved
preliminary plat for conformity with recommended revisions. If approved, the
plat shall be forwarded to the city council.
   (C)   Fees: The following fees shall accompany the final plat when presented
to the city council for approval: (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
      1.   Filing Fees: As set by resolution pursuant to section
1-5-3 of this code. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975; amd. 1977 Code; Ord. 375, 5-11-1995)
      2.   Copies At Subdivider's Expense: One copy each shall be provided to
the county surveyor, county assessor, city engineer and city clerk. (Ord. 266,
4-10-1975)
CHAPTER 4
PRINCIPLES OF ACCEPTABILITY
SECTION:
6-4-1: Principles Enumerated
6-4-1: PRINCIPLES ENUMERATED:
   (A)   Summary: The street layout for each subdivision shall be based on the
sections of the master plan adopted or proposed for the city and shall be
considered in relation to existing and planned streets, to topographic
conditions, to public convenience and safety, and shall have an appropriate
relation to the proposed uses of the land to be served by such streets. Where
such is not shown on the master plan, the arrangement of streets in a
subdivision shall either:
      1.   Provide for the continuation or appropriate projection of existing
streets in surrounding areas; or
      2.   Conform to the plan for the neighborhood approved or adopted by the
city council to meet a particular situation where topography or other
conditions make continuance or conformance to existing streets impracticable.
   (B)   Intersections, Along Arterial Streets: Intersections of residential or
collector streets with arterial streets and highways shall, insofar as
practicable, be widely spread along the arterial streets and be limited in the
number of intersections to the minimum necessary for reasonable convenient
access between arterial streets and local neighborhood areas.
   (C)   Future Extension Of Streets: Where a subdivision adjoins unsubdivided
land, streets which, in the opinion of the city council, should be continued in
the event of the subdivision of the adjoining land, will be required to be
provided to the boundary lines of the tract.
   (D)   Partial Development: Where the plat to be subdivided contains only
part of the tract owned by the subdivider, the city council shall require a
sketch of a tentative future street system for the unsubdivided portion.
   (E)   Acreage Tract: Where a tract of land is subdivided into large parcels,
the arrangement of lots and streets shall be so as to permit a resubdivision
into smaller lots in conformity with the street and lot requirements specified
in these regulations. Building setback lines shall be established in order to
preserve future rights of way.
   (F)   Frontage On Arterial Streets: Where a subdivision abuts or contains an
existing or proposed arterial street, the city council may require frontage
streets, reverse frontage lots with a minimum depth of one hundred fifty feet
(150'), screen planting contained in a nonaccess reservation along the rear
property line, or such other treatment as may be necessary for adequate
protection of residential properties and to afford separation of through and
local traffic.
   (G)   Half Street: Half streets may be approved when essential to the
reasonable development of the subdivision when in conformity with the other
requirements of these regulations; and when the city council finds it will be
practicable to require the dedication of the other half when the adjoining
property is subdivided. Whenever a half street is adjacent to a tract to be
subdivided, the other half of the street shall be platted within such tract.
Half streets will not be constructed until both sides have been platted.
   (H)   Street Names: No street names shall be used which will duplicate or be
confused with the names of existing streets. Street names shall be subject to
the approval of the city council and shall conform to the street name and
pattern established by ordinance and from the official city map.
   (I)   Reserved Strips: Reserved strips or street plugs controlling the
access to public ways will not be approved unless such strips are necessary for
the protection of the public welfare or of substantial property rights, or
both, and in no case unless the control and disposal of the land comprising
such strips is placed definitely within the jurisdiction of the city under
conditions approved by the city council. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
CHAPTER 5
DIMENSION AND LAYOUT REQUIREMENTS
SECTION:
6-5-1: General Requirements
6-5-1: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   Minimum Right Of Way Widths: Street right of way widths shall be shown
on the master plan and, where not shown thereon, shall be adequate for the type
of street indicated by its function in the design of the land and subdivision.
   (B)   Width: Width of rights of way shall meet the minimum requirements
shown in the following table:
 
Type Of Street                                           Right Of Way Minimum
Arterial street                                          80 feet
For multi-family or commercial development and collector 80 feet
streets
Residential street                                       50 feet
Cul-de-sac (dead end street with turnaround)             50 feet
Turnaround for cul-de-sac                                40 foot radius
Alley                                                    20 feet
 
   (C)   Intersections:
      1.   Horizontal Intersection Angle: Ninety degree (90°) preferred;
seventy five degree (75°) minimum.
      2.   Sight Distance: The city council may require such conditions as will
establish and protect adequate sight distances for vehicular traffic at street
intersections.
   (D)   Curves: When connecting street lines deflect from each other at any
one point by more than ten degrees (10°), they shall be connected by a curve
with a radius adequate to ensure traffic safety and proper street construction
and appearance.
   (E)   Blocks: The lengths, widths and shapes of blocks shall be designed
with due regard to:
      1.   Building Sites: Provision of adequate building sites suitable to the
special needs of the type of use contemplated.
      2.   Traffic: Needs for convenient access, circulation, control and
safety of street traffic.
      3.   Topography: Limitations and opportunities of topography.
   (F)   Lots:
      1.   Dimensions: Lot dimensions shall in all cases conform to the minimum
requirements of the zoning regulations for the district.
      2.   Side Lot Lines: The side lines of lots shall run at right angles to
the street on which the lots face, as far as is practicable, or on curved
streets shall be radial to the curve as far as practicable.
      3.   Double And Reverse Frontage: Double frontage and reverse frontage
lots shall be avoided except where essential to provide separation of
residential development from traffic arteries or to overcome specific
disadvantages of topography and orientation.
      4.   Lots Subject To Resubdivision: In subdividing tracts which at some
future time are likely to be resubdivided, the location of lot lines and other
details of the layouts shall be such that resubdivision may readily take place
without violating the requirements of these regulations and without interfering
with the orderly development of streets. Restrictions of buildings within
future street locations shall be made a matter of record if the city council
considers it necessary.
      5.   Intersections: Property lines at intersections shall be rounded with
a minimum radius of ten feet (10'), or shall have comparable cutoffs or chords
in place of rounded corners.
   (G)   Easements For Utility Lines: Easements for sewer, water, gas,
electric, telephone, drainage, irrigation or other public utilities shall be
required. Easements for utility lines shall be a minimum of fifteen feet (15')
in width, and centered on rear or side lot lines.
   (H)   Watercourses: Where a subdivision is traversed by a watercourse,
including irrigation ditches and canals, drainageway, channel or stream, there
shall be provided an easement of such width adequate to carry the water and to
construct and maintain the waterway.
   (I)   Alleys:
      1.   Location: Alleys shall be provided in commercial and industrial
districts, unless other access to off street parking and loading facilities are
made, as approved by the city council.
      2.   Intersections: Alley intersections and sharp changes in alignment
shall be avoided, but, where necessary, corners shall be cut off sufficiently
to permit safe vehicular movement.
      3.   Dead Ends: Dead end alleys shall be avoided where possible but if
unavoidable, shall be provided with adequate turnaround facilities as
determined by the city council.
   (J)   Sewage System: In subdivisions within the city, method and extent of
sewage disposal shall meet with the standards of and be approved by the city.
In subdivisions within one mile of the city, method and extent of sewage
disposal shall meet the standards of and be approved by the appropriate state
and federal agencies having jurisdiction over such matters. In a subdivision
within a reasonable distance to an existing sanitary system, the subdivider may
be required to make connection thereto.
   (K)   Land Surface Drainage: Such grading shall be done and such structure
shall be provided by the subdivider as are deemed essential by the city
engineer to provide adequate drainage. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
CHAPTER 6
REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
6-6-1: Minimum Street Requirements
6-6-2: Minimum Sewer Line Requirements
6-6-3: Minimum Water Line Requirements
6-6-4: Pipe Sizes
6-6-5: Plans
6-6-6: Responsibilities
6-6-1: MINIMUM STREET REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   Forty foot (40') wide asphalt concrete surface two inches (2") thick;
one-half inch (1/2") or three-fourths inch (3/4") maximum aggregate approved by
the city council.
   (B)   Minimum eight inches (8") compacted crushed aggregate base; six inches
(6") of one and one-half inches (11/2") minus and two inches (2") of three-
fourths inch (3/4") minus.
   (C)   Compacted subgrade.
   (D)   Two percent (2%) crown minimum.
   (E)   Provide curb and gutter as typical. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
6-6-2: MINIMUM SEWER LINE REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   Minimum three inch (3") asbestos cement.
   (B)   Minimum grade of four-tenths percent (0.4%).
   (C)   Thirty six inch (36") minimum depth.
   (D)   To be located ten feet (10') right or left of street or alley
centerline.
   (E)   Services to be stubbed by city to property lines before street
construction. Saddles required.
   (F)   Trenches to be water settled or mechanically compacted.
   (G)   Standard manholes required at all angle points, both vertical and
horizontal.
   (H)   Standard manhole covers with dust pans. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
6-6-3: MINIMUM WATER LINE REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   Minimum of six inch (6") asbestos cement.
   (B)   Minimum thirty six inch (36") depth. At least one foot (1') depth
difference from sewer line.
   (C)   Located ten feet (10') left or right of street centerline.
   (D)   Service to be stubbed to property line by city. Corporation and curb
stops required.
   (E)   Trenches to be water settled or mechanically compacted.
   (F)   Loop connection mains where possible.
   (G)   Gate valves at beginning and end of main as required by the
circumstances.
   (H)   One fire hydrant and valve for every one hundred twenty five thousand
(125,000) square feet of subdivision to be placed as directed by the city.
   (I)   Risers required on all gate valves and curb stops. (Ord. 266, 4-10-
1975)
6-6-4: PIPE SIZES:
Any pipe sizes required by the city larger than above set forth will be
compensated for on proportional basis by the city. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
6-6-5: PLANS:
Three (3) sets of plans for sewer, water and street construction shall be
prepared at the expense of the subdivider by a registered professional engineer
and shall be submitted to the city public works director for approval prior to
construction. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
6-6-6: RESPONSIBILITIES:
The subdivider shall be responsible and pay for all expenses in connection with
the subdivision, including engineering, construction of streets and alleys,
construction of water lines, sewer, drains, curbs, gutters, sidewalks and fire
hydrants, whether the subdivision is within or outside the city limits. All
engineering shall conform to city standards. The city engineer or public works
director, at the expense of the subdivider, shall be responsible for inspection
of public utilities and all streets, alleys, water lines, sewers, drains,
curbs, gutters, sidewalks and fire hydrants, and all of the same shall be
constructed and installed by the subdivider to conform to all city ordinances
and state laws. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
CHAPTER 7
VARIATIONS AND EXCEPTIONS
SECTION:
6-7-1: Council Powers
6-7-2: Conditions
6-7-1: COUNCIL POWERS:
Where the city council finds that extraordinary hardship may result from strict
compliance with these regulations, it may vary the regulations so that
substantial justice may be done and the public interest secured; provided, that
such variation will not have the effect of nullifying the intent and purpose of
the master plan of the city. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
6-7-2: CONDITIONS:
In granting variances and modifications, the city council may require such
conditions as will, in their judgment, secure substantially the objectives of
the standards or requirements so varied or modified. (Ord. 266, 4-10-1975)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION; PUBLIC WAYS 1
SECTION:
7-1-1: Definitions
7-1-2: Permit Requirements
7-1-3: Construction Regulations
7-1-4: Owner Responsible For Condition Of Sidewalks
7-1-5: Street Grades
7-1-6: Installation And Construction Specifications
7-1-7: New Buildings; Curbs And Sidewalks Required
7-1-8: Obstructing Streets
7-1-9: Responsibility For Improvements
 
Notes
1 1. Note: A certified copy of this chapter shall be recorded in the office of
  the county recorder of Gooding County, Idaho.
7-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
OWNER: Any form of legal or equitable ownership, whether individual, firm,
partnership or corporation, or in any other fiduciary, legal or equitable
capacity.
PUBLIC SIDEWALKS: For the purpose of this chapter and establishing owner's
responsibility shall be those public sidewalks abutting the owner's property or
those adjacent public sidewalks located between the owner's property frontage
lines and the adjacent public street curb lines. In those locations where there
is no curb, the responsibility of the said property owner for said repairs
shall extend to the edge of the nearest public traffic lanes. (Ord. 339, 8-14-
1986)
7-1-2: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   (A)   No public sidewalk shall be repaired or installed by any person
without first having a written permit from the city. A permit shall cover only
contiguous construction and the work to be done as one continuous operation.
   (B)   A permit shall expire for work not started within forty five (45)
days, or completed within one hundred eighty (180) days after the issuance of a
permit. (Ord. 339, 8-14-1986)
7-1-3: CONSTRUCTION REGULATIONS:
   (A)   Construction And Grade Specifications: Applicant shall follow the
provisions required by the City of Wendell or their representative for sidewalk
construction and grade.
   (B)   Variances: The City Council may authorize variances from standard
sidewalk provisions where no curb exists or when unusual topographical
conditions, nature of existing construction, or similar factors would make
adherence to standard provisions unreasonable.
   (C)   Inspection Of Work: All work shall be subject to inspection by the
city during construction and upon completion. No concrete shall be poured
without the permit and approval of the City of Wendell. (Ord. 339, 8-14-1986;
amd. Ord. 551-2023, 6- -2023)
7-1-4: OWNER RESPONSIBLE FOR CONDITION OF SIDEWALKS:
   (A)   Repair And Replacement: All owners or agents of owners with property
abutting or fronting upon any plaza or street within the corporate limits of
the city, are required to keep the public sidewalks in good order and repair.
Each such owner shall be liable to the city for all losses to the city or
recoveries from the city for damages to persons or property of others caused by
his failure or that of his agents, to keep in good order and reasonably safe
condition, all such sidewalks fronting his property upon any plaza or street
within the corporate limits of the city. The city may, at its discretion,
through the superintendent of streets and alleys, notify such owner that
repairs or replacements are necessary to put such sidewalks in good order and
such owner shall, within thirty (30) days after such notification, under the
supervision of the building inspector, complete such repairs or replacements as
specified in such notice. If the person fails to make the required repairs or
replacements, the city may repair or replace same, at their sole discretion,
and the owner shall be liable to the city for the cost of the repair or
replacement, and such costs shall be a lien and encumbrance against the
property in favor of the city. If the city takes such action in connection with
repair or replacement and recording a lien against the property, the city clerk
is authorized to file and certify such lien with the county recorder of Gooding
County, Idaho, and such charge will be a proper charge and lien against the
owner's property as mentioned. If such charges are not paid within thirty (30)
days after recording of same with the Gooding County recorder, the city clerk
shall, at the discretion and direction of the mayor and city council, certify
such charges, with a copy to the delinquent owner, to the treasurer of Gooding
County, Idaho, to be placed on the tax rolls of Gooding County for collection,
and the same shall be collected in the same manner and with like effect and
subject to the same charges and penalties as other taxes.
   (B)   Ice, Snow And Debris Removal: Each of said sidewalk owners shall also
be responsible for and it shall be his or her duty, to clear his or her
sidewalk of accumulations of ice, snow, debris, or any other encroachments
which unreasonably interfere with the use of the sidewalks by the general
public. If the city, at its sole discretion, elects to clear any such sidewalk
of ice, snow, debris or obstructions as mentioned, then the city may declare a
lien against the abutting property for costs of such removal and clearance.
Such lien may be charged and collected as mentioned above, in connection with
repair of sidewalks. (Ord. 339, 8-14-1986)
7-1-5: STREET GRADES:
All permanent sidewalks ordered constructed under the provisions of this
chapter shall be built on the grade established by the city for the street or
streets on which the same are built, which grades shall be furnished to the
property owners by the city engineer. Streets shall be constructed in good and
workmanlike manner, under the supervision of the city engineer and in
accordance with detailed specifications furnished by him. (Ord. 35, 5-8-1914)
7-1-6: INSTALLATION AND CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS:
Sidewalks and crosswalks shall be installed and constructed with such materials
and in such manner as are set forth in the specifications of the city engineer
on file in the office of the city clerk, or in such specifications as may be
hereafter filed by the city engineer. (1977 Code)
7-1-7: NEW BUILDINGS; CURBS AND SIDEWALKS REQUIRED:
   (A)   It is the purpose and intent of this section to establish the policy
and procedure that no new buildings for residential or business purposes shall
be erected without the construction of curbs, gutters and sidewalks and being
installed in conjunction with the construction of such buildings.
   (B)   No building permit for the construction of any building for
residential or business purposes shall hereafter issue unless the application
therefor contains an adequate description of the plans and specifications for
the construction and installation of curbs, gutters and sidewalks.
   (C)   If sixty percent (60%) or more of the total property length adjacent
to the property on a standard block does not have existing curb and gutter, the
construction of curb and gutter may be deferred unless it will connect to an
existing curb and gutter section. Calculation of the amount of existing curb
and gutter shall include the length of the property in question. The standard
block shall be the distance between two (2) intersecting streets or four
hundred feet (400'), whichever is less. This same sixty percent (60%) criteria
shall separately apply to the requirement for sidewalks. All curb and gutter to
be considered as existing shall be to acceptable line and grade.
   In the event it appears that this subsection is applicable, the application
for building permit shall contain a covenant by the applicant that the
construction of such curb, gutter and sidewalk shall be constructed by the
applicant or his successors in interest upon demand by the city. Demand may be
made by the city at any time when it appears that buildings have been
constructed upon sixty percent (60%) or more of the block as first herein
provided, whether or not curb, gutter and sidewalks have been constructed in
connection therewith.
   (D)   All such curbs, gutters and sidewalks shall be constructed and
installed in accordance with the provisions of this chapter and title 4,
chapter 1 of this code, and such provisions are hereby amended, respectively,
to the extent necessary to effectuate the purposes and intent of this section.
   (E)   Any person violating any of the provisions of this section shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and each such person shall be deemed guilty of
a separate offense for each and every day or portion thereof during which the
violation of the provisions of this section is committed, continued or
permitted. (Ord. 293, 10-27-1977)
7-1-8: OBSTRUCTING STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct or cause to be obstructed any
public street, alley, sidewalk or bridge or to render inconvenient to pass; to
continue such obstruction as to dig up any street, alley, sidewalk or public
ground within the city without the authority of the mayor, or to place, leave
or cause to be placed or left in any street, alley or sidewalk any wagon, cart,
sleigh, dray, barrow, handcart or other vehicle, or any lumber, wood or timber
or other article or thing whatsoever, in such manner as to obstruct or
interfere with the public use of any street, alley or sidewalk, or to fence or
to fill in or remove any earth or other material from any street, alley or
sidewalk or interfere therewith except by permission of the mayor, or to throw,
cast or lay any ashes, offal, shavings, dirt, filth, soapsuds, filthy water or
rubbish of any kind whatsoever in any street, sidewalk, watercourse, ditch,
lane, alley or place within the city, except as may be designated by the city
authorities. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
7-1-9: RESPONSIBILITY FOR IMPROVEMENTS:
   (A)   Definitions: As used herein:
   EXISTING DEVELOPMENT: Those areas which have met the following conditions
for a period of at least five (5) years:
      1.   Have been within the city limits;
      2.   Have had all public and private streets serving the development
graded and open to the public;
      3.   Have had fifty one percent (51%) or more of the area within the
development boundary occupied by buildings.
   NEW DEVELOPMENT: All areas within the jurisdiction of the city not defined
as "existing development".
   (B)   Responsibility Of Landowners: Landowners in new development shall be
obligated for all costs of engineering and construction of service facilities,
and all such engineering and construction shall be in accordance with the terms
and provisions of the subdivision title of the city, and as the same may be
hereafter amended and supplemented.
   (C)   Responsibility Of City: The city shall bear the costs and
responsibility of engineering in existing developments. The city and landowners
shall be obligated for construction costs pertaining to streets, pavement of
streets, installation of streetlights, fire hydrants, curbs and gutters,
sidewalks, water lines, sewer and storm sewers and similar improvements in such
proportions and amounts as may be established from time to time by resolution
of the city establishing policies for such construction and development.
This section shall not apply to developments which are substantially in
progress as of the effective date hereof. (Ord. 292, 10-27-1977)
CHAPTER 2
OPEN GRAVITY WASTEWATER SYSTEM
SECTION:
7-2-1: Regulation By City
7-2-2: Permit Required For Discharge
7-2-3: Application For Permit
7-2-4: Water Quality Determination
7-2-5: Compliance With Regulations
7-2-6: Discharge Without Permit, Nuisance
7-2-1: REGULATION BY CITY:
It is hereby declared to be in the best interests of the inhabitants of the
city, and in the preservation of public health, and to promote the general
welfare, that the control of discharge of water or other waste into the open
gravity wastewater system of the city be controlled and upon terms and
provisions as fixed by the city. (Ord. 259, 3-28-1974)
7-2-2: PERMIT REQUIRED FOR DISCHARGE:
No person shall hereafter permit, allow or suffer any water, liquids of any
nature or other waste to be discharged into any portion of the open gravity
wastewater system of the city, as now or hereafter constructed, without having
first obtained a permit from the city for such discharge. (Ord. 259, 3-28-1974)
7-2-3: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Any person desiring to discharge any water, liquid or other waste into the
gravity wastewater system of the city shall make application for permission so
to do to the city clerk, and no such permit shall issue except upon the
approval thereof by the mayor and city council. (Ord. 259, 3-28-1974)
7-2-4: WATER QUALITY DETERMINATION:
The mayor and city council shall not issue any such permit unless and until a
determination is made that the water quality of the matter sought to be so
discharged is of an equal or better quality than that presently being conveyed
in the said gravity wastewater system of the city. If any valid rules or
regulations of any federal, state or county are then in effect, prescribing
standards of water quality discharged by the city, anyone seeking a permit
shall establish that the applicant will not cause, permit or suffer any
discharge from applicant's property into the city wastewater system not
satisfying such rules, standards or regulations. (Ord. 259, 3-28-1974)
7-2-5: COMPLIANCE WITH REGULATIONS:
It is hereby declared that it shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any
waste into any part of the gravity wastewater system of the city, except as
herein provided. (Ord. 259, 3-28-1974)
7-2-6: DISCHARGE WITHOUT PERMIT, NUISANCE:
The discharge of any such water into the gravity wastewater system of the city,
without having obtained a permit, as herein provided, is hereby declared to be
a nuisance. (Ord. 259, 3-28-1974)
CHAPTER 3
SEWER USE REGULATIONS; RATES
SECTION:
7-3-1: Purpose
7-3-2: Definitions
7-3-3: Application Of Provisions
7-3-4: Use Of Public Sewers
7-3-5: Injury To Sewerage System Unlawful
7-3-6: Permission To Discharge Objectionable Waste Or Water
7-3-7: Powers And Authority Of City
7-3-8: Basis For Determining Sewer User Charges
7-3-9: Rate Change Request
7-3-10: Purpose Of Monthly Sewer User Charge
7-3-11: Monthly Rates
7-3-12: Sewer Connection Required
7-3-12.1: Extensions
7-3-13: Rates And Charges
7-3-14: Nonpayment, Lien
7-3-15: Privies, Cesspools Restricted
7-3-16: Penalty
7-3-1: PURPOSE:
It is hereby determined and declared to be necessary and conducive to and for
the protection of the health, safety and welfare of the public and inhabitants
of the city, and for the purpose of controlling the use and for providing an
equitable distribution of the costs and expenses of maintenance, operation,
upkeep and repair of the entire sewerage treatment system, which includes the
pump lift station, sewage lagoons and land disposal facilities of the city, to
charge and collect service charges or fees upon all lots, lands, property and
premises served or benefited by the sewerage system of the city, which system
and facilities consist generally of all pipelines, conduits, manholes, clean
outs, sewer mains, intercepting sewers, outfall sewers, lift stations, pumps,
structures, mechanical equipment and facilities for the treatment and disposal
of sewage or sewage byproducts. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meaning of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND (BOD): The quantity of oxygen utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in
five (5) days at twenty degrees Celsius (20°C), expressed in milligrams per
liter (mg/l).
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five
feet (5') outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to a point of connection
with the public sewer or other place of disposal.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from the domestic and commercial preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food, and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: The liquid wastes from industrial manufacturing processes,
trade or business as distinct from sanitary sewage.
MULTIPLE BUILDING DEVELOPMENT: Includes the various types of developments that
would have common or joint ownership areas such as condominiums, townhouses,
mobile home parks or courts, shopping centers, etc.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface or ground water.
pH: The logarithm of the recripocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food that have been shredded to such a degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") in any dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights, and is controlled by public authority.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which storm, surface and
ground waters are not intentionally admitted.
SERVICE CONNECTION: The point at which the building sewer connects to the
public sewer.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water carried wastes from residences, business
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such
ground, surface and storm waters as may be present.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
SEWAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of
sewage.
SEWER: A pipe or conduit for carrying sewage.
SEWER USER: Any individual, firm, company, association, society or corporation,
or group who has connected to the sewerage system.
SHALL, MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissive.
SLUG: Any discharge of water, sewage or industrial waste which in concentration
of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of
duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5) times the average
twenty four (24) hour concentration or flows during normal operation.
STORM DRAIN (Sometimes Termed STORM SEWER): A sewer which carries storm and
surface water and drainage, but excludes sewage and industrial wastes, other
than unpolluted water such as cooling water.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension in water, sewage or other liquids, and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-3: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
The provisions of this chapter shall apply to all property within the corporate
limits of the city, and any special users outside of the corporate limits of
the city, including all property owned or occupied by the United States of
America, Gooding County and the state of Idaho. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-4: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS:
The use of the public sewers of the city shall be in accordance with the
following regulations:
   (A)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any storm water,
surface water, ground water, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated
cooling water or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer.
   (B)   Storm water and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to
such sewers as are specifically designated as storm sewers, or to a natural
outlet approved by the city. Industrial cooling water or unpolluted process
waters may be discharged, on approval of the city, to a storm sewer or natural
outlet.
   (C)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following described waters or wastes to any public sewers:
      1.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas.
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids
or gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other
wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a
hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance, or create any hazard in
the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant, including, but not limited
to, cyanides in excess of two milligrams per liter (2 mg/l) as CN in the wastes
as discharged to the public sewer.
      3.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5, or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment
and personnel of the sewage works.
      4.   Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of
causing obstruction to flow in sewers, or other interference with the proper
operation of the sewage works, such as, but not limited to, ashes, cinders,
sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar, plastics, wood,
unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and fleshings, entrails and
paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole or ground by garbage
grinders.
   (D)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged the following
described substances, materials, waters or wastes if it appears likely, in the
opinion of the city, that such wastes can harm either the sewers, sewage
treatment process or equipment, have an adverse effect on the receiving stream,
or can otherwise endanger life, limb, public property or constitute a nuisance.
In forming its opinion as to the acceptability of these wastes, the city will
give consideration to such factors as the quantities of subject wastes in
relation to flows and velocities in the sewers, materials of construction of
the sewers, nature of the sewage treatment process, capacity of the sewage
treatment plant, degree of treatability of wastes in the sewage treatment
plant, and other pertinent factors. The substances prohibited are:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (65°C).
      2.   Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oils, whether
emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter (100 mg/l) or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures
between thirty two degrees Fahrenheit (32°F) and one hundred fifty degrees
Fahrenheit (150°F) (0° and 65°C).
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths (3/
4) horsepower or greater shall be subject to the review and approval of the
city.
      4.   Any waters or wastes containing strong acid iron pickling wastes or
concentrated plating solutions whether neutralized or not.
      5.   Any waters or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc and
similar objectionable or toxic substances; or wastes exerting any excessive
chlorine requirement, to such degree that any such material received in the
composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established
by the city for such materials.
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste or odor
producing substances in such concentrations exceeding limits which may be
established by the city as necessary, after treatment of the composite sewage,
to meet the requirements of the state, federal or other public agencies of
jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters.
      7.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half life or
concentration as may exceed limits established by the city in compliance with
applicable state or federal regulations.
      8.   Any waters or wastes having a pH in excess of 9.5.
      9.   Materials which exert or cause:
         (a)   Unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids (such as, but
not limited to, fuller's earth, lime slurries and lime residues) or of
dissolved solids (such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride and sodium
sulfate).
         (b)   Excessive discoloration (such as, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions).
         (c)   Unusual BOD, chemical oxygen demand, or chlorine requirements in
such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment
works.
         (d)   Unusual volume of flow or concentration of wastes constituting
"slugs", as defined herein.
      10.   Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to
treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment process employed, or are
amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant
effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction
over discharge to the receiving waters.
   (E)   If any waters or wastes are discharged, or are proposed to be
discharged to the public sewers, which waters contain the substances or possess
the characteristics enumerated in subsection (D) of this section, and which, in
the judgment of the city, may have a deleterious effect upon the sewage works,
processes, equipment or receiving waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to
life or constitute a public nuisance, the city may:
      1.   Reject the wastes;
      2.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the
public sewers;
      3.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/or
      4.   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating the
wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges under the provisions of
section
7-3-8 of this chapter. If the city permits the pretreatment or equalization of
waste flows, the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be
subject to the review and approval of the city and subject to the requirements
of all applicable codes, ordinances and laws.
   (F)   Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the
opinion of the city, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid
wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand or
other harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be required
for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a
type and capacity approved by the city, and shall be located as to be readily
and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection.
   (G)   Where preliminary treatment or flow equalizing facilities are provided
for any waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory
and effective operation by the owner at his expense.
   (H)   When required by the city, the owner of any property serviced by a
building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable control
manhole, together with such necessary meters and other appurtenances in the
building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and measurement of the
wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessibly and safely located,
and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by the city. The
manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense, and shall be maintained
by him so as to be safe and accessible at all times.
   (I)   All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters
and wastes to which reference is made in this chapter shall be determined in
accordance with the latest edition of "Standard Methods For The Examination Of
Water And Wastewater", published by the American Public Health Association, and
shall be determined at the control manhole provided, or upon suitable samples
taken at said control manhole. In the event that no special manhole has been
required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream
manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is
connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily accepted methods to
reflect the effect of constituents upon the sewage works and to determine the
existence of hazards to life and property.
   (J)   No statement contained in this chapter shall be construed as
preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city and any
industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character
may be accepted by the city for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the
industrial concern.
   (K)   Any property owner or sewer user violating the provisions of this
section shall, upon notice by the city, immediately install such preliminary
treatment through separators, traps and/or chemical, physical or biochemical
processes as will make and assure that the sewage contributed from such
property or premises will meet the requirements of this chapter. (Ord. 268, 5-
22-1975)
7-3-5: INJURY TO SEWERAGE SYSTEM UNLAWFUL:
   (A)   No unauthorized person shall maliciously, wilfully or negligently
break, damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure,
appurtenance or equipment which is a part of the sewerage works.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit any garbage, rubbish,
dead animals or any substance having a tendency to obstruct the flow of the
sewer in any manhole, clean out or sewer opening. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-6: PERMISSION TO DISCHARGE OBJECTIONABLE WASTE OR WATER:
The admission into the public sewers of any water or wastes having: a)
biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) greater than three hundred milligrams per liter
(300 mg/l); or b) suspended solids in excess of three hundred milligrams per
liter (300 mg/l), shall be subject to the review and approval of the city.
Where necessary, in the opinion of the city, the owner shall provide, at his
expense, such preliminary treatment as may be necessary to reduce the BOD to
three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l) and the suspended solids to three
hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l). Plans, specifications and any other
pertinent information relating to proposed preliminary treatment facilities
shall be submitted for the approval of the city and of the state department of
health, and no construction of such facilities shall be commenced until said
approvals are obtained in writing. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-7: POWERS AND AUTHORITY OF CITY:
   (A)   The city, through its authorized representative bearing proper
credentials and identification, shall be permitted to enter all properties for
the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling and testing in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter. The city shall have no
authority to inquire into any processes, including metallurgical, oil,
refining, ceramics, paper or other industries beyond that point having a direct
bearing on the kind and source of discharge to the sewers or natural waterways.
   (B)   While performing the necessary work on private properties referred to
hereinabove in this section, the authorized representative of the city shall
observe all safety rules applicable to the premises established by the sewer
user and the sewer user shall be held harmless for injury or death to any city
authorized representative, and the city shall indemnify the sewer user against
loss or damage to its property by any authorized city representative and
against liability claims and demands for personal injury and property damage
asserted against the sewer user growing out of the gauging and sampling
operation, except as such may be caused by negligence or failure of the sewer
user to maintain safe conditions as required in this chapter.
   (C)   The city, through its authorized representative bearing proper
credentials and identification, shall be permitted to enter all private
properties through which the city holds a duly negotiated easement for the
purposes of, but not limited to, inspection, observation, measurement,
sampling, repair and maintenance of any portion of the sewerage works lying
within said easement. All entry and subsequent work, if any, on said easement,
shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement
pertaining to the private property involved. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-8: BASIS FOR DETERMINING SEWER USER CHARGES:
   (A)   Rates: The sewer user rate shall be based on the following equivalent
user schedule, "one equivalent user" defined as contributing two hundred sixty
(260) gallons per day, and fifty five-hundredths (0.55) pound of five (5) day
BOD per day to the sewer system:
 
USER EQUIVALENT SCHEDULE
Single-family residences     1 equivalent user
Churches                     1 equivalent user
Mobile home or trailer house 1 equivalent user
Offices                      1 equivalent user
Multiple living units1       1 equivalent user per apartment
Special users2               Not applicable
 
   Notes:
      1.    This basis of charge applicable to multiple living unit not
designated as a special user.
      2.    Each special user shall be evaluated separately based on the flow
and BOD characteristics of the sewage discharged to the sewer. A copy of the
list of special users, the characteristics of their sewage and the user charge
for each shall be kept on file at all times in the office of the city clerk.
   Charges for sewage treatment operation, maintenance and replacement shall be
computed in the following manner:
   DEFINITION OF VARIABLES:
   A =   Anticipated yearly expense
   B =   Total daily BOD to treatment facilities
   C =   Chemical expenses
   D =   Daily BOD from a special user
   E =   Electrical expenses
   F =   Total daily wastewater flow to treatment facility
   G =   Total daily BOD from special users
   H =   Total daily wastewater flow from special users
   I =   Total daily BOD from equivalent users
   J =   Total daily wastewater flow from equivalent users
   K =   Fraction allocable to wastewater flow
   L =   Labor and equipment expenses for O&M
   M =   Monitoring and testing expenses
   N =   Number of equivalent users
   O =   Additional anticipated yearly expenses
   P =   Previous year expenses
   Q =   Daily wastewater flow from a special user
   R =   Replacement sinking fund
   S =   Total number of special users
   T =   Total number of sewer users
   U =   Daily wastewater flow per user equivalent
   V =   Daily BOD per user equivalent
   W =   Cost per unit of flow
   X =   Cost per # BOD/day
   Y =   Yearly cost for each equivalent user
   Z =   Monthly equivalent user rate
   AA =   Total yearly cost allocable to wastewater flow
   BB =   Total yearly cost allocable to BOD
   CC =   Total yearly cost for a special user
   A=P+O = C+E L+M+R
ALLOCATION OF COSTS
Type Of Cost Flow BOD
ALLOCATION OF COSTS
Type Of Cost        Flow   BOD
Chemical            K1 x C (1-K1) x C
Electrical          K2 x E (1-K2) x E
Labor and equipment K3 x L (1-K3) x L
Monitoring          K4 x M (1-K4) x M
Replacement         K5 x 4 (1-K5) x R
Sum total           AA     BB
 
   W = AA/F   ) Yearly unit costs for BOD and flow computation
         )
   X = BB/F   )
   COMPUTATION OF MONTHLY EQUIVALENT USER COSTS
      N =    T - S
      J =    F - H
      I =    B - G
      U =    J + N
      V =    I + N
      Y =    W x U + X x V
      Z =    Y + 12
   COMPUTATION OF MONTHLY USER COSTS
      Yearly BOD cost special user = D x W
      Yearly flow cost special user = Q x W
      Sum total          CC
      Monthly special user rate = CC + 12
   Revisions to the user charges shall be based upon actual operation,
maintenance and replacement expenses and/or a significant change in the total
number of equivalent users, total daily BOD and/or total daily flow to the
sewage treatment facilities. As a minimum, the user charge for operation,
maintenance and replacement will be reviewed annually and updated to reflect
actual costs.
   The city may install a measuring device in the sewer service line at any
time to determine the amount of wastewater and/or collect wastewater samples
for testing. After measuring and/or sampling, the city may adjust the user
charge to conform to actual usage. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975; amd. Ord. 519-2013, 3-
7-2013)
   (B)   Determine Equivalent Residential Units:
      1.   Equivalent Residential Units:
         (a)   Each property connecting to city of Wendell's potable water
system and/or wastewater system shall be assigned an equivalent residential
unit (ERU), or multiple thereof.
            (1)   All single-family residential properties connecting to city
services are assigned one ERU.
            (2)   All master metered multi-family residential properties
connecting to city services shall be assigned appropriate ERUs as indicated by
equivalent residential unit table.
            (3)   All properties connecting to city services which are not
residential properties will be assigned, by the public works director, city
administrator or an engineered study, an ERU multiple based upon the property's
estimated daily water consumption (in gallons). A division will be calculated
to the second decimal place and rounded according to mathematical convention.
In no event shall a nonresidential property be assigned an ERU of less than
one.
         (b)   The city of Wendell's potable water system and wastewater system
capacity fees are set by resolution by the Wendell city council annually or as
needed.
         (c)   The ERU multiple established for nonresidential properties based
on estimated water consumption shall be reviewed twelve (12) months after
occupancy to determine if the estimated daily water consumption is accurate.
Any increase or decrease in the ERU multiple based on actual water consumption
shall be corrected and communicated to the property owner in writing.
      2.   Restricted Funds:
         (a)   All potable water system capacity fees shall be deposited into
the city's potable water capacity fee fund.
         (b)   All wastewater sewer system capacity fees shall be deposited
into the city's wastewater sewer capacity fee fund.
         (c)   Funds collected pursuant to this subsection shall be expended
only for system improvements.
         (d)   The city of Wendell's potable water system and wastewater system
capacity fees are set by resolution by the Wendell city council on an annual
basis or as needed.
      3.   Appeal To City Council:
         (a)   An ERU determination by the city public works director, city
administrator, or engineered study shall be final unless a written notice of
appeal to the city council is filed with the city of Wendell within twenty (20)
days of the date of such ERU determination.
         (b)   The appeal must include the names of all witnesses, including
experts that will testify in support of appellant's appeal with a summary of
the testimony of each witness or expert.
         (c)   The appeal shall be heard by the city council not more than
ninety (90) days after the appeal is filed by the appellant. The decision of
the city council shall be reflected in council meeting minutes. (Ord. 519-2013,
3-7-2013)
7-3-9: RATE CHANGE REQUEST:
Any user feeling aggrieved at the user charge for OM&R may request that his
charge be changed if:
   (A)   Flow proportioned BOD tests certified by an independent laboratory
specializing in wastewater analysis indicates significant deviation in BOD5
from the value used by the city in computing the BOD charge; and/or
   (B)   Total daily wastewater flow measurements derived from a continuously
recording measuring device and certified by an authorized representative of the
city as to their authenticity indicate a significant deviation in wastewater
flow from the value used by the city in computing wastewater flow charge;
   (C)   The flow measurement and testing methods are approved in detail by the
city prior to actual measurement and testing.
All changes in user charges applicable to this chapter shall be computed by the
method outlined in this chapter. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975)
7-3-10: PURPOSE OF MONTHLY SEWER USER CHARGE:
   (A)   The monthly sewer user charge is established to cover operation and
maintenance costs of the treatment system, and to provide a fund, to pay for
replacement costs.
   (B)   For new construction, the sewer user charge is to begin when the
service connection has been inspected and approved or when the building being
served is substantially completed, whichever is the latest date. (Ord. 268, 5-
22-1975)
7-3-11: MONTHLY RATES:
   (A)   Monthly rates for the various classifications of sewer users defined
in section
7-3-8 of this chapter shall be established by the city council through
resolutions to that effect and shall be kept on file at all times in the office
of the city clerk1.
   (B)   Effective June 1, 2005, only real property owners of property served
by the city services may subscribe to city utility services, including water,
sewer and sanitation. The property owner shall be considered the “water user”,
“sewer user” and “sanitation user”. Notwithstanding the above, language, a
tenant of real property may complete an application for utility services for
real property rented by the tenant and receive bills for utilities furnished to
said real property, where the real property owner has completed an application
for utility services to said real property and the real property owner has
consented in writing to a lien on said real property for the nonpayment of
utility services furnished to the real property. (Ord. 268, 5-22-1975; amd.
Ord. 448, 4-7-2005; Ord. 561-2025, 1-2-2025)
7-3-12: SEWER CONNECTION REQUIRED:
   (A)   Requirements: All owners of property, tenants and other occupants of
real property within the municipal areas within the city of Wendell, Idaho, and
within two hundred feet (200') of the general sewerage system of the city, and
within the areas physically capable of receiving the services of the system of
sewerage in the city, shall, within ninety (90) days after a notice signed by
the city clerk requiring connections to be made with such sewerage system,
cause connections to be made between said sewerage system and their respective
properties. All connections of said sewer system heretofore constructed and
made shall be maintained in a sanitary, permanent and watertight condition. All
connections made hereafter shall be made in a permanent and sanitary manner and
shall be sufficient to carry all the sewerage and waste fluids of every kind
from the building into said system of sewage, and each toilet, sink, stationary
washstand and other piece or type of equipment having waste fluids, shall be
connected with said system; provided, that where the building or structure has
not been completed before such notice, connection shall be made on or before
completion of such building or structure and before any occupancy or use
thereof.
   (B)   Failure To Repair; Action By City; Lien: If any connection or any
needed repair to an existing condition shall not be made within the time herein
provided, the city council is hereby authorized and directed to cause the same
to be made and to file a statement of the costs thereof with the city clerk,
and thereupon a warrant shall be issued under the direction of the city council
by the city treasurer for the payment of such cost. The amount of such cost,
together with a penalty of ten dollars ($10.00), plus interest at eight percent
(8%) per annum upon the total amount of such costs and penalty, shall be
assessed against the property upon which the said building or structure is
situated and shall become a lien thereon as hereafter provided. (Ord. 454A, 3-
7-2013)
7-3-12.1: EXTENSIONS:
   (A)   All proposed water and/or sewer line extensions to the municipal water
and/or sewer supply of the city shall be first presented to the city council by
application, and all such extensions must be approved by the city council prior
to the commencement of construction.
   (B)   All new water and/or sewer line extensions in the city shall be
installed by the city staff unless otherwise approved by the city council.
   (C)   No water mains less than six inches (6") in diameter shall be
installed within the city service area without the approval of the city
council. No sewer mains less than eight inches (8") in diameter shall be
installed within the city service area without the approval of the city
council.
   (D)   The city may, at the sole discretion of the city council, pay for
water and/or sewer line extensions.
   (E)   The city may also participate in the costs of such extensions by
providing labor, material or other types of cost sharing, all at the sole
discretion of the city council.
   (F)   The city may also enter into agreements to reimburse those persons or
entities that have provided, or will provide, such extensions.
   (G)   Subsections (A) through (F) of this section apply to water and/or
sewer extensions within the corporate boundaries of the city. In the event any
person or other entity desires sewer and/or water extensions or hookups to the
city systems, outside the boundaries of the city limits, an application, in a
form approved by the city council, must be completed and the city council shall
have absolute discretion to either allow, disallow or allow with contingencies,
such extensions. All such extensions must meet city and state standards in
effect at the time of installation and shall be inspected by the city engineer
or city superintendent. The cost of such inspections shall be the
responsibility of the person or entity requesting city services, unless
otherwise waived by the city council.
      1.   Any person or entity desiring such extension shall sign an agreement
for connection to the city water and/or sewer system for property owners
outside of the corporate limits of the city. Such agreement shall provide for
the annexation of the property being served at the option of the city.
      2.   The person or entity desiring such extension shall agree to provide
for such extension at their own expense.
   (H)   "As built" or "record" drawings of water line and/or sewer line plans
shall be prepared by a professional engineer and the "corrected" original
drawing or duplicate mylar copy of the "corrected" original drawing shall be
provided to the city. Such drawing shall be signed by the professional engineer
in charge of the work stating that such drawing is true and correct and that
the job site has been inspected. (Ord. 393, 1-8-1997)
7-3-13: RATES AND CHARGES:
   (A)   The monthly minimum rates and charges are hereby fixed by resolution
for sewer service in the city and shall be paid monthly by said owners, tenants
or occupants, and said rates commencing ninety (90) days after the city clerk
has sent notice, whether the connection is made or not, to their respective
properties or to their successors in interest. An owner of real property will
be connected to the city sewer as stated above; it is the property owner's
responsibility from the sewer main line to the residence or other building.
   (B)   All connections made with the sewer system after completion of the
construction of the general system shall be at the expense of the individual
owner or user, and must be made under direct supervision of an authorized city
official, and an inspection fee as fixed by resolution shall be paid by each
such individual for such connection with the sewer.
   (C)   The city council hereby expressly reserves the right to change or
revise the rates by resolution. (Ord. 454A, 3-7-2013)
7-3-14: NONPAYMENT, LIEN:
   (A)   All charges for connections and for sewerage service provided for in
this chapter, together with penalties and interest thereon, shall be a lien
upon the property with which such connection is made or sewerage service
rendered respectively, superior to all other liens and encumbrances whatsoever
except for general taxes and local special assessments. The city treasurer is
hereby authorized and directed, prior to the expiration of six (6) months from
the first day of the first month for which such charges were unpaid, to certify
to the auditor of Gooding County, Idaho, all of such charges as a lien upon
such property. Said lien will be placed according to the provisions of ldaho
Code section 50-1008 after thirty (30) days of nonpayment of utilities when
due. Notice of delinquency will be sent to the property owner via mail within
five (5) days of the City's certification of a lien amount under Idaho Code
section 50-1008. Payment, notice, hearings and redemption for said lien will
follow the provisions of Idaho Code Title 63, Chapter 10.
   (B)   As an additional and concurrent method of enforcing the lien of the
city for said charges, the city council is hereby authorized and directed at
the end of five (5) days after the date of the first delinquency of any such
charges to shut off the water and sewer services from the premises to which
such services were furnished, and said services shall remain shut off until all
such charges, plus penalties and interest thereon, shall be paid.
   (C)   Utility bills are past due if not paid by five o’clock (5:00) p.m. on
the twentieth (20th) day of the month. When the twentieth (20th) day of the
month falls on a Saturday, Sunday or legal holiday, the utility bill will be
considered due on the next day that is not a Saturday, Sunday or legal holiday.
By eight o’clock (8:00) a.m. on the twenty-first (21st) day of the month,
unless that day is a Saturday, Sunday or legal holiday, a two percent (2%)
penalty will automatically be added to all unpaid balances. (Ord. 454A, 3-7-
2013; amd. Ord. 561-2025, 1-2-2025)
7-3-15: PRIVIES, CESSPOOLS RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to dig, or use, or cause to be dug, or
used, any privy vault or cesspool, or connect any plumbing with a cesspool, or
build, or cause to be built, any privy building within the limits of the city
of Wendell, except upon written permit by the city council. All applications
for such permits must be in writing and accompanied by a certificate from the
city council that said premises are not within two hundred feet (200') of a
public sewer. (Ord. 454A, 3-7-2013)
7-3-16: PENALTY:
Any violation of this chapter shall, upon conviction of a misdemeanor thereof,
be punished by a fine in any sum not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00),
or by imprisonment not to exceed thirty (30) days in the county jail, or by
both said fine and imprisonment. (Ord. 454A, 3-7-2013)

  waterworks.
7-4-1: USE OF CITY WATER REQUIRED:
   (A)   It is hereby declared to be in the best interest of the inhabitants of
the city; and in the preservation of public health; and to promote the general
welfare that it be provided that a single source of water supply for domestic,
culinary and industrial purposes be maintained and operated within the limits
of the city.
   (B)   It is hereby declared that it shall be unlawful for any person to use
water for any domestic, culinary or industrial purpose which water is not
obtained from the municipal waterworks of the city.
   (C)   The use of any such water from a source other than the municipal
waterworks of the city is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
   (D)   If, in the opinion of the mayor and city council, it is determined to
be physically impossible or economically prohibitive for any such inhabitant to
connect to and use water from the municipal waterworks, upon application and
good cause shown therefor, a waiver may be granted by the mayor and city
council and such inhabitant may be permitted to obtain such water from some
other source. (Ord. 255, 2-28-1974)
7-4-2: WATERWORKS FUND:
   (A)   Records: It shall be the duty of the city treasurer to keep an
accurate record of all funds turned over to him by the superintendent of
waterworks in a separate fund to be known as the "waterworks fund".
   (B)   Disbursements: All disbursements for the operation and maintenance of
the waterworks system and repair thereof shall be paid out of said fund upon
warrants duly drawn by the mayor and city clerk, and all bills shall be first
approved by the superintendent and passed and allowed by the city council
before warrants therefor shall be drawn on said fund. In case there is a
surplus in said fund over and above the cost of operation, maintenance and
repair of the system, it may be used for the extension of said system if so
ordered by the city council. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-3: APPLICATION FOR WATER, CONDITIONS:
   (A)   Form: All applications for the use of water shall be made upon printed
blanks to be provided by the city, and signed by the applicant. All applicants
shall agree to be governed by such rules and regulations as may be subscribed
by the city council for the management of the system. Such application shall
state the location by street name, lot and block number of the property for
which service is desired, and it shall be unlawful for any person supplied with
water from said waterworks system to furnish to, or supply, any other person
with water except as covered in said application.
   (B)   Discontinuance: Any person desiring to discontinue use of water shall
give notice in writing thereof to the superintendent. No reduction or abatement
of water rates shall be made unless such notice is given, nor for a period of
less than one month.
   (C)   Deposit: The application shall be accompanied by a security deposit,
in such amount as the city council may from time to time establish. A security
deposit is required each time a new "water user," "sewer user," or "sanitation
user" completes an application for water and/or sewer services, unless the
applying user has made timely payment of utilities for twelve consecutive
months. No more than one security deposit at one time will be required for a
given report to receive utility services. If a security deposit is refunded.
pursuant to the terms established by city resolution. the individual or entity
that paid the deposit shall receive the refund of said deposit.
   (D)   Real Property Owner Responsible: Effective June 1, 2005, only real
property owners of property served by the city services may subscribe to city
utility services, including water, sewer and sanitation. The property owner
shall be considered the “water user”, “sewer user” and “sanitation user”. (Ord.
324, 10-8-1981; amd. Ord. 448, 4-7-2005; Ord. 561-2025, 1-2-2025)
7-4-4: CONNECTION CHARGES:
The service pipes and connections from the main to the lot line, including a
curb box, meter and meter box, to be placed within the line of the street curb,
will be put in and maintained by the water department, and kept within its
exclusive control, for which charges shall be as set by resolution pursuant to
section
1-5-3 of this code. (Ord. 359, 11-21-1991; amd. Ord. 375, 5-11-1995)
7-4-5: SCHEDULE OF RATES ESTABLISHED:
   (A)   Rates: It shall be the duty of the city council, by order or
resolution duly passed and entered upon the minutes of said city council, to
fix and establish a schedule of rates for the supply of water from the said
waterworks system, which rates shall be payable as provided in section
7-4-6 of this chapter. And the city council may, in the same manner from time
to time, alter, change or amend said schedule of rates; provided, that no such
change shall be made except at a regular meeting of the city council, or at a
meeting called for that special purpose, of which all members shall have been
given due notice. The said rates shall, in every case, cover but one user, lot,
premises, family or firm. (Ord. 324, 10-8-1981; amd. Ord. 519-2013, 3-7-2013)
   (B)   Determine Equivalent Residential Units: See subsection
7-3-8(B) of this title. (Ord. 519-2013, 3-7-2013)
7-4-6: PAYMENT OF BILLS 1 :
The superintendent of waterworks shall, before the first day of each calendar
month, furnish to each user of water from the waterworks system a statement of
the minimum amount due the city for the use of the water for the previous
month, in accordance with the schedule of rates established and in force in the
city. All water rates shall be due and payable on the twentieth of each month,
and unless paid by the twentieth of the month, shall be delinquent, and it
shall be the duty of the superintendent to cause the water to be turned off
from all such delinquent users, and before the water shall be turned on again,
all delinquent rates must be paid in full, plus an additional fee, as set by
resolution pursuant to section
1-5-3 of this code, for expense. (Ord. 359, 11-21-1991; amd. Ord. 375, 5-11-
1995; Ord. 548-2023, 3- -2023)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  8-2-10 of this code, billing for water along with sewer and garbage charges.
7-4-7: SEPARATE CONNECTIONS:
Service pipes must be so arranged that the supply of each separate water user,
house or premises may be controlled by a separate stopcock and meter, and
before water will be supplied through such service pipe, the owner of the
property for which service is rendered must agree to be responsible for and pay
for all water used through such service. Where water is now supplied through
one service to one or more houses or persons, the city council may, in their
discretion, either refuse to furnish water until separate service for each user
is provided, or may continue the supply on the condition that one person shall
agree to be responsible for and pay for all water used through such service.
(Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-8: SERVICE PIPE SPECIFICATIONS:
All service and other pipes used underground shall be of cast iron, steel or
extra strong lead or tin lined lead (except private pipes where the use of
special material may be authorized) laid not less than three feet (3') below
the surface of the ground and of sufficient strength to stand the water
pressure. All work upon the alteration or extension of water pipes and size of
pipes shall be subject to the approval of the superintendent of the waterworks;
and no extensions shall be made to another water user from the same service
without a stopcock and meter being attached to the junction of such service
pipe. No consumer shall be permitted to conduct water pipes across lots or
through or under buildings to adjoining premises, but all service pipes shall
enter the premises at a point nearest the water main. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-9: FIRE HYDRANTS, DRINKING FOUNTAINS:
All fire hydrants and public drinking fountains shall be under the supervision
and control of, and shall be kept in repair by, the superintendent of
waterworks. The fire department shall at all times have free access to the fire
hydrants. Water may also be furnished from the fire hydrants for sprinkling
streets, flushing wagons and other purposes, under the supervision of the
superintendent. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-10: SHUT OFF FOR REPAIRS:
The superintendent of waterworks may, at any time, shut off the water from the
various water mains of said system for the purpose of making repairs or
extensions to said system or for other good reasons, and no claim shall be made
against the city by reason of the breakage of any service pipe, service cock or
meter or for any damage that may result from so shutting off the water;
provided, the superintendent shall have authority to only shut off the water
when necessary, and shall turn the water on again within a reasonable time.
(Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-11: PROTECT PIPES FROM FREEZING:
All water users shall keep their service pipes, connections and other apparatus
in good order and repair and protect them from freezing at their own expense;
and no person, except under the direction of the superintendent, shall be
allowed to dig into the streets or sidewalks for the purpose of laying,
removing or repairing any service pipes. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-12: FREE ACCESS TO PREMISES:
Free access shall, at all ordinary hours, be allowed to the superintendent or
other person authorized by him to all places and premises supplied with water
from the waterworks system, to examine the apparatus, read meters or any other
necessary and legal purpose. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
7-4-13: METER ACCURACY:
The superintendent of waterworks shall have power to adjust all erroneous bills
and correct any errors occurring in meter readings, or in rendering of
statements. In case of any dispute about the accuracy of any meter, the
superintendent shall check out such meter and test the same. If the meter is
found to be inaccurate, it shall be adjusted without charge to the consumer,
but if found to be accurate, a charge, as set by resolution pursuant to section
1-5-3 of this code, shall be made to the consumer for testing the meter. The
superintendent shall report all such corrections and adjustments to the city
council monthly, or more often if required. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914; amd. Ord.
375, 5-11-1995)
7-4-14: APPLICATION TO EXTEND WATER LINES:
   (A)   All proposed water and/or sewer line extensions to the municipal water
and/or sewer supply of the city shall be first presented to the city council by
application, and all such extensions must be approved by the city council prior
to the commencement of construction.
   (B)   All new water and/or sewer line extensions in the city shall be
installed by the city staff, unless otherwise approved by the city council.
   (C)   No water mains less than six inches (6") in diameter shall be
installed within the city service area without the approval of city council. No
sewer mains less than eight inches (8") in diameter shall be installed within
the city service area without the approval of the city council.
   (D)   The city may, at the sole discretion of the city council, pay for
water and/or sewer line extensions.
   (E)   The city may also participate in the costs of such extensions by
providing labor, material or other types of cost sharing, all at the sole
discretion of the city council.
   (F)   The city may also enter into agreements to reimburse those persons or
entities that have provided, or will provide, such extensions.
   (G)   Subsections (A) through (F) of this section apply to water and/or
sewer extensions within the corporate boundaries of the city. In the event any
person or other entity desires sewer and/or water extensions or hookups to the
city systems, outside the boundaries of the city limits, an application, in a
form approved by the city council, must be completed, and the city council
shall have absolute discretion to either allow, disallow or allow with
contingencies, such extensions. All such extensions must meet city and state
standards in effect at the time of installation and shall be inspected by the
city engineer or city superintendent. The cost of such inspections shall be the
responsibility of the person or entity requesting city services, unless
otherwise waived by the city council.
      1.   Any person or entity desiring such extension shall sign an agreement
for connection to the city water and/or sewer system for property owners
outside of the corporate limits of the city. Such agreement shall provide for
the annexation of the property being served at the option of the city.
      2.   The person or entity desiring such extension shall agree to provide
for such extension at their own expense.
   (H)   "As built" or "record" drawings of water line and/or sewer line plans
shall be prepared by a professional engineer and the "corrected" original
drawing or duplicate Mylar copy of the "corrected" original drawing shall be
provided to the city. Such drawing shall be signed by the professional engineer
in charge of the work stating that such drawing is true and correct and that
the job site has been inspected. (Ord. 393, 1-8-1997)
7-4-15: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The city council shall, from time to time, adopt such further rules and
regulations governing the management and control of said waterworks system, and
the distribution and use of water therefrom as they shall deem best and
necessary and such rules and regulations, when duly adopted, shall have the
same force and effect as if incorporated in an ordinance of the city. (Ord. 39,
12-15-1914)
7-4-16: UNLAWFUL ACTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, other than those duly authorized, to
perform any of the following acts:
   (A)   To open, operate, tamper or interfere with, or in any manner obstruct
the approach to any fire hydrant.
   (B)   To hitch any vehicle or animal to any fire hydrant or public drinking
fountain.
   (C)   To have in his possession, or to use, or permit to be used any wrench
for any fire hydrant for any other purpose than that authorized by the
superintendent of the waterworks system.
   (D)   To destroy, deface, injure or in any way tamper with any meter, meter
box, stop cock, valve or check, or the pumps, machinery or any apparatus
connected with the operation of said waterworks system.
   (E)   For any water user to permit any person from other premises, or any
unauthorized person to use or obtain water from his premises or water fixtures,
whether inside or outside of his buildings.
   (F)   For any person, by himself, family, servants or agents to use the
water coming through the water mains without first paying therefor as herein
provided, or without authority to open any stop cock, valve or other apparatus
attached to said system of waterworks.
   (G)   For any person, after the water has been turned off from his premises
on account of nonpayment of rates, or other violation of the rules and
