regulations pertaining to the use of water, to turn on, or allow the water to
be turned on, or to use or allow to be used, water from said system, without
authority from the superintendent of waterworks.
   (H)   To violate or disobey any of the provisions of this chapter or any of
the rules and regulations in force governing the management, operation and
distribution of water from said waterworks system. (Ord. 39, 12-15-1914)
CHAPTER 6
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES
SECTION:
7-6-1: Purpose And Scope
7-6-2: Definitions
7-6-3: Cross Connections
7-6-4: Service
7-6-5: Violations And Penalties
7-6-6: Severability
7-6-1: PURPOSE AND SCOPE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the public health of domestic water
users receiving their water supply from the city. (Ord. 319, 12-11-1980)
7-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
BACKFLOW: The flow of nonpotable water, liquids, gases, or other foreign
substances into the pipes of a potable water system from any source or sources.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: The device to counteract back pressure or to
prevent back siphonage.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any actual or potential connection or structural arrangement
between a public or a consumer's potable water system to any other source or
system through which it is possible to introduce into any part of the potable
system, used water, industrial fluid, gas or substance other than the intended
potable water with which the system is supplied. Bypass arrangements, jumper
connections, removable sections, swivel or change over devices and any other
temporary or permanent devices which or because of which "backflow" can or may
occur are cross connections. (Ord. 319, 12-11-1980)
7-6-3: CROSS CONNECTIONS:
No water service connection shall be installed or hereafter maintained unless
the water supply is protected by backflow prevention devices as required by the
rules and regulations of the Wendell water department as the same now exists or
as may be hereafter amended or supplemented. Any such cross connection now
existing or hereafter installed is hereby declared a public nuisance and shall
be abated. (Ord. 319, 12-11-1980)
7-6-4: SERVICE:
Service to any property, landowner or water consumer receiving a water supply
from the city water supply system shall be contingent upon compliance with all
the requirements of the rules and regulations of the water department and of
this chapter pertaining to cross connections. Service shall be discontinued to
any premises, water consumer or property owner for failure to comply with such
regulations of the water department and of this chapter pertaining to cross
connections, and any discontinued service will not be reestablished until the
city or its designated agent has approved compliance by that particular
premises or water consumer or landowner. (Ord. 319, 12-11-1980)
7-6-5: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects, refuses to comply with, or
resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this chapter or the rules
and regulations as adopted by the city in connection herewith, shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 319, 12-11-1980)
7-6-6: SEVERABILITY:
If any one or more sections, subsections, or sentences of this chapter are for
any reason held to be unconstitutional or invalid, such decisions shall not
affect the validity of the remaining portions of this chapter and the same
shall remain in full force and effect. (Ord. 319, 12-11-1980)
CHAPTER 7
TREES AND SHRUBS 1
SECTION:
7-7-1: Definitions
7-7-2: Responsibilities
7-7-3: Permit Required
7-7-4: Variance
7-7-5: Prohibited
7-7-6: Violation; Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 2, chapter 4 of this code.
7-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
COMMUNITY FOREST: All trees within the city.
PUBLIC TREE: Any tree on a public right of way or city owned property, or any
tree whose limbs, roots or trunk encroach upon a public right of way or upon
city owned property.
STREET TREES: Trees along a public right of way, sidewalks or streets and
alleyways or trees whose branches, roots or trunks encroach upon the city right
of way, including alleyways. (Ord. 434, 11-18-2003)
7-7-2: RESPONSIBILITIES:
   (A)   Property Owners: Owners of property adjacent to a street tree shall
provide adequate maintenance for the tree. Adequate maintenance shall include
sufficient water, proper pruning and protection from injury by vehicles or
other causes.
   (B)   City:
      1.   The city shall remove or cause the removal of public or private tree
branches which present a hazard to the public health, safety or welfare.
      2.   The city shall have the right to plant, prune, maintain and remove
trees, plants or shrubs within the right of way of all streets, alleys, and
public grounds. (Ord. 434, 11-18-2003)
7-7-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
Permits shall be required for property owners to remove, prune or plant any
street trees. Permits shall be issued only if it has been established to the
city's satisfaction that there is a need for action and the person so doing has
adequate safety measures in place and adequate insurance. (Ord. 434, 11-18-
2003)
7-7-4: VARIANCE:
Any variance from this chapter shall be applied for as any other variance
pursuant to this code. (Ord. 434, 11-18-2003)
7-7-5: PROHIBITED:
   (A)   It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to abuse,
destroy, poison or mutilate any public tree, plant, shrub, or the roots of any
public tree, plant or shrub.
   (B)   It shall be a violation of this chapter to top any public tree. (Ord.
434, 11-18-2003)
7-7-6: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine
not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) per occurrence. (Ord. 434, 11-18-
2003)
CHAPTER 8
WATER CONSERVATION
SECTION:
7-8-1: Best Practices Of Water Use
7-8-2: Additional Stages 1 - 3 Restrictions
7-8-3: Additional Restrictions
7-8-4: Duration Of Restrictions
7-8-5: Exceptions
7-8-6: Alternate Water Management Plans
7-8-7: Violations And Fines; Appeals
7-8-1: BEST PRACTICES OF WATER USE:
   (A)   The following minimum standards, considered the foundation of "best
practices of water use", are encouraged and recommended by the city of Wendell:
      1.   Increase public awareness of the water supply situation and provide
educational materials about best practice of water use.
      2.   Encourage the entire community to conserve water whenever possible.
      3.   Eating establishment, restaurant, hotel, cafe, cafeteria, etc.,
should not serve drinking water unless expressly requested by a patron and
should display notice of such policy.
      4.   Hotels will provide notice of declared water conservation programs
and encourage conservation practices.
      5.   All city facilities will limit use of potable water for the watering
of landscape to three (3) days a week.
      6.   Vehicles should be washed only on scheduled watering day.
      7.   Landscape watering using potable water is restricted to the
following schedule:
   Even numbered addresses: even number calendar days.
   Odd numbered addresses: odd number calendar days.
   Premises with no street address, such as a median: even number calendar
days.
      8.   Watering will only be allowed on appropriate irrigation days before
ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. or after five o'clock (5:00) P.M.
      9.   Outdoor landscape watering with a drip irrigation system or handheld
container is allowed at any time.
      10.   Sprinkler systems must be maintained in a manner that promotes
efficient watering and limits leaks or damage to the system that would allow
flow of water beyond property lines.
      11.   Customers are encouraged to use irrigation water rather than
potable water for watering landscape when and where available. (Ord. 491, 2-21-
2008)
7-8-2: ADDITIONAL STAGES 1 - 3 RESTRICTIONS:
When deemed appropriate based on evaluation of projected water supply and
demand, the city council may move by resolution to implement additional
restrictions as outlined in stages 1 - 3.
Stage 1:
   (A)   No water customer shall apply water to impervious surfaces such as
streets, sidewalks, patios, decks, etc.
   (B)   Landscape watering using potable water two (2) days per week on
designated days:
      1.   City facilities are restricted to two (2) days a week.
      2.   Even numbered addresses: Tuesday and Saturday.
      3.   Odd numbered addresses: Wednesday and Sunday.
      4.   Premises with no street address, such as a median: Monday and
Friday.
Stage 2:
   (A)   No water customer shall apply water to impervious surfaces such as
streets, sidewalks, patios, decks, etc.
   (B)   Landscape irrigation one day a week:
      1.   City facilities are restricted to one day a week.
      2.   Even numbered addresses: Tuesday.
      3.   Odd numbered addresses: Friday.
      4.   Premises with no street address, such as a median: Monday.
Stage 3:
   (A)   No water customer shall apply water to impervious surfaces such as
streets, sidewalks, patios, decks, etc.
   (B)   Indoor use may be reduced by a percentage to be determined by the city
council.
   (C)   Landscape watering using potable water two (2) days per month on
designated days.
      1.   City facilities are restricted to one day a week during the first
and third weeks of the month.
      2.   Even numbered addresses: second and fourth Tuesday.
      3.   Odd numbered addresses: first and third Friday.
      4.   Premises with no street address, such as a median: second and fourth
Monday. (Ord. 491, 2-21-2008)
7-8-3: ADDITIONAL RESTRICTIONS:
   (A)   Based upon evaluations of the expected yield and projected demands the
city council may impose additional restrictions on water use during any stage
including, but not limited to, any of the following:
      1.   No additional water connections to the system allowed - moratorium
on building permits.
      2.   Outdoor water prohibited except for large trees with trunks of at
least six inches (6") in diameter.
      3.   Operation of water features prohibited.
      4.   Filling or refilling of water features, pools and ponds prohibited.
(Ord. 491, 2-21-2008)
7-8-4: DURATION OF RESTRICTIONS:
The city shall conduct regular evaluations of the expected yield and projected
demands to determine whether it is necessary to continue the water use
restrictions. If water supply conditions warrant, restrictions may be either
downgraded or withdrawn subject to city council approval by resolution. (Ord.
491, 2-21-2008)
7-8-5: EXCEPTIONS:
Water customers may use water essential to protect the general public health,
safety or welfare. Irrigation systems may be operated at any time for
maintenance purposes (not to exceed 10 minutes per station). Customers may
apply for relief from watering schedules for purposes of establishing a new
lawn not to exceed three (3) months. (Ord. 491, 2-21-2008)
7-8-6: ALTERNATE WATER MANAGEMENT PLANS:
A water customer may request relief from applicable restrictions by filing an
alternative water management plan with the city of Wendell, public works
director. The city of Wendell will provide customers with the ability to design
water management alternatives that give customers flexibility in meeting the
restrictions while achieving maximum conservation goals. The city must give
approval to the plan, may require periodic reporting, and posted notice of
alternate water management plans. (Ord. 491, 2-21-2008)
7-8-7: VIOLATIONS AND FINES; APPEALS:
   (A)   Each water customer shall be responsible for compliance with this
chapter with respect to the water customer's premises and shall be responsible
for applicable fines for noncompliance with this chapter. In the event of an
alleged violation of this chapter, proof of the existence of a declared water
shortage and proof of any violation of any restriction set forth in this
chapter, together with proof that the violation originated at any water
customer's premises shall constitute a rebuttal presumption that the water
customer is responsible for the violation.
   (B)   Fines through stage 2:
      1.   First violation: Written warning.
      2.   Second violation: Written notice and add a forty dollar ($40.00)
fine to the water bill of the premises.
      3.   Third violation: Written notice and add an eighty dollar ($80.00)
fine to the water bill for the premises.
      4.   Fourth violation and subsequent violations: Written notice and add a
one hundred twenty dollar ($120.00) fine to the water bill for the premises.
   (C)   Fines through stage 3:
      1.   First violation: Written notice and add an eighty dollar ($80.00)
fine to the water bill for the premises.
      2.   Second violation: Written notice and add a one hundred sixty dollar
($160.00) fine to the water bill for the premises.
      3.   Third and subsequent violations: Written notice and add a two
hundred forty dollar ($240.00) fine to the water bill for the premises.
   (D)   Any fine assessed shall be added to the customer's water bill.
   (E)   Any appeal of a fine imposed may be appealed within fifteen (15) days
of the billing date through the city of Wendell public works director. Any
decision of the city of Wendell public works director may be appealed to the
city council within fifteen (15) days of the decision. Appeals must be written
and addressed to the city of Wendell water department.
   (F)   Written warning or notice shall be delivered in person to the
customer's premises by leaving it with a person at the premises, over the age
of eighteen (18) years, or posting on the front door if no one is present to
accept it.
   (G)   Any unpaid fines shall be applied to the property tax of the premises.
(Ord. 491, 2-21-2008)
TITLE 8
HEALTH AND SANITATION
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
8-1-1: Abandoned Vehicles, Equipment And Personal Property
8-1-2: Defined; Enumerated
8-1-3: Abatement Procedures
8-1-4: Penalty For Violation
8-1-1: ABANDONED VEHICLES, EQUIPMENT AND PERSONAL PROPERTY:
No person in charge of or in control of any premises, whether as owner, lessee,
tenant, occupant or otherwise, shall allow any partially dismantled, wrecked,
junked, discarded or otherwise nonoperating and unlicensed motor vehicle,
machinery, farm implement, equipment and/or personal property of any kind,
which is no longer safely usable for the purposes for which it was
manufactured, to remain on such property longer than twenty eight (28) days,
unless such vehicle, equipment or other property, is maintained in an enclosed
building or so located within a fenced or screened enclosure of at least six
feet (6') in height, in accordance with, and as defined by, the zoning
ordinance and building codes of the city, such that the materials are not
readily visible from any public place or from any surrounding private property.
Allowing such materials to remain unenclosed or unscreened shall constitute a
nuisance. This section shall not apply with regard to any vehicle, equipment or
other personal property on the premises of a business enterprise operated in a
lawful place, other than in a residential district, and operated in a lawful
manner, when the keeping or maintenance of such vehicle, equipment or other
damaged and abandoned personal property is necessary to the operation of such
business enterprise and is not in violation of other provisions of law. (Ord.
428, 6-26-2002)
8-1-2: DEFINED; ENUMERATED:
For the purposes of this chapter, the term "nuisance" is defined to mean any
condition or use of premises or of building exteriors which is detrimental to
the property of others or which causes or tends to cause substantial diminution
in the value of other property in the neighborhood in which such premises are
located. This includes, but is not limited to, the keeping or the depositing
on, or the scattering over the premises of any of the following:
   (A)   Useless lumber, junk, trash or other debris.
   (B)   Abandoned, inoperable, discarded or unused objects or equipment such
as automobiles, implements and/or equipment, machinery, appliances and personal
property of any kind which is no longer safely usable for the purposes for
which it was manufactured, furniture, stoves, refrigerators, freezers, cans or
containers.
   (C)   Any compost pile or liquid/semiliquid waste which is of such a nature
as to spread or harbor disease, emit unpleasant odors or harmful gas, or
attract rodents, vermin or other disease carrying pests, animals or insects;
provided, that the presence of earthworms in a compost pile shall not
constitute a nuisance, nor shall a properly maintained garden compost facility.
   (D)   Keeping unsanitary matter on premises. It shall be unlawful for any
person to keep or permit another to keep upon any premises deleterious or
septic material which causes adverse effects upon the occupancy or use of
neighboring lands. Such materials must generally be retained in containers or
vessels which deny access by humans, flies, insects, rodents and animals.
   (E)   All offensive and noxious weeds or plants, within the limits of the
city, are hereby declared to be a public nuisance and shall be removed, cut and
destroyed by the owner or agent of the ground or premises on which the same are
located. It shall be the duty of the owner, agent or person having charge of
any property within the city limits where offensive or noxious weeds or plants
are growing to remove, cut and/or destroy the same. This shall include all
rights of way abutting the property which they own, are an agent, or have
charge of. (Ord. 428, 6-26-2002)
8-1-3: ABATEMENT PROCEDURES:
   (A)   Prior to initiating prosecution for violation of this chapter, city
staff shall attempt to provide notice to the owner of the real property upon
which the nuisance is located. Additional notice shall be attempted to the
occupant/tenant or agent if one is known. Said notice shall describe the
location of the property as accurately as possible and shall specify the nature
of the nuisance and the time by which the nuisance must be abated. Said notice
shall be mailed to the owner, agent, person in charge of such property, if such
owner, agent or person in charge can be found. If an owner, agent or person in
charge cannot be found, then notice shall be provided by posting a notice in a
conspicuous place on the premises and mailing a copy of said notice by
certified mail to the owner or agent of the same at such owner's or agent's
last known address.
   (B)   The owner, owners, tenants, lessees and/or occupants of any lands upon
which a nuisance is located may thereafter store such nuisance vehicles,
equipment or materials into completely enclosed buildings authorized to be used
for such storage purposes, if within the corporate limits of the city, or
otherwise remove the vehicles, equipment or materials to a lawful storage
location outside the corporate limits of the city. If the nuisance consists of
weeds or other vegetative materials, it shall be removed and disposed of
lawfully so as to eliminate the fire hazard created and/or the risk of spread
of weed infestation.
   (C)   The provisions of this chapter shall not compromise or otherwise
adversely affect the applicability of provisions of Idaho law regarding the
designation of nuisances and their abatement. (Ord. 428, 6-26-2002)
8-1-4: PENALTY FOR VIOLATION:
   (A)   If the owners, tenants or occupants allow said nuisance to exist or
fail to abate the nuisance, they, and each of them, shall be guilty of an
infraction and upon being found liable therefor shall be subject to an
infraction penalty of one hundred dollars ($100.00). Each day that a violation
of this chapter exists may be charged as a separate infraction or misdemeanor
violation, as appropriate. Any nuisance which violates this chapter and which
constitutes an immediate hazard to the public health or which continues to
exist after a finding of guilt or liability in two (2) or more prior infraction
proceedings, shall constitute a misdemeanor subject to a fine of up to three
hundred dollars ($300.00) or imprisonment for up to one hundred eighty (180)
days, or by both such fine and imprisonment.
   (B)   In the event the property owner fails, refuses or neglects to abate
such nuisance as identified by the city for a period of more than thirty (30)
days; the city shall cause the same to be abated and such costs shall be placed
upon the tax rolls of the property owner pursuant to Idaho Code section 50-317.
(Ord. 428, 6-26-2002)
CHAPTER 2
GARBAGE AND RUBBISH
SECTION:
8-2-1: Purpose
8-2-2: Definitions
8-2-3: City Right To Collect, License
8-2-4: Collection Prohibited By Unauthorized Persons
8-2-5: Vehicles Hauling Garbage
8-2-6: Discarding Garbage, Rubbish
8-2-7: Sweeping Debris Into Streets, Free Access To Alleys
8-2-8: Rules And Regulations
8-2-9: Garbage Containers Required; Specifications, Placement
8-2-10: Garbage Service Rates
8-2-11: Water Shut Off For Nonpayment
8-2-12: Civil Action To Collect
8-2-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter shall be deemed an exercise of the police power of the city acting
in its governmental capacity, for the protection and preservation of the
health, welfare, morals, safety and cleanliness of said city and all its
provisions shall be liberally construed for the accomplishment of that purpose.
(Ord. 197, 12-21-1962)
8-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter:
GARBAGE: Includes and means kitchen and table refuse and offal, swill and also
every accumulation of animal, fruit or vegetable matter, liquid or otherwise,
that attends the preparation, consumption, use, decay, cooking, dealing in or
storage of animal matter, meats, fish, fowl, birds, fruits or vegetables
(saving and excepting that dead animals exceeding 10 pounds in weight and offal
of slaughterhouses are not included within the meaning of the word "garbage" as
herein defined). The word "garbage" does not include dishwater or wastewater.
All wet garbage shall be kept in separate containers not to exceed fifty (50)
pounds' gross weight.
RUBBISH: Includes and means ashes, broken crockery, broken bottles, broken
bricks, tin vessels, trimmings from lawns and flower gardens, including
shrubbery, pasteboard boxes, berry boxes, paper sacks, straw, packing
materials, shavings, discarded household utensils, but the term "rubbish" shall
not include broken or discarded stoves or furniture, broken or discarded
building materials, trees or any waste accumulated, other than heretofore
specified. The term "ashes" shall be held to include and mean the residue of
materials burned. This rubbish can be placed in boxes or cans provided no
container weighs more than fifty (50) pounds; gross. (Ord. 156, 7-7-1950)
8-2-3: CITY RIGHT TO COLLECT, LICENSE:
   (A)   The city, its duly authorized agents, contractors, servants, employees
or licensees shall have the exclusive right to gather and collect garbage and
rubbish within the city, and it shall be unlawful for any person, except as
otherwise provided in this chapter, to collect or gather garbage and/or rubbish
within the city.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person, other than the city, its agents
and employees, or a person holding a permit or license issued by the city for
such purpose, to collect or convey, through, over or upon any street or alley
within the city, any garbage. (Ord. 197, 12-21-1962)
8-2-4: COLLECTION PROHIBITED BY UNAUTHORIZED PERSONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, other than the city, its agents or
employees or a person holding a permit or license for such purpose, or having a
contract with the city for such purpose, to interfere in any manner with any
receptacle containing garbage or rubbish or any form of refuse, or to remove
any such receptacle from the location where the same was placed by the owner
thereof, or to remove any of the contents of such receptacle. (Ord. 197, 12-21-
1962)
8-2-5: VEHICLES HAULING GARBAGE:
Every vehicle used to cart or haul garbage or rubbish in, about, along, over or
upon any street, alley, highway or thoroughfare of the city, shall be fitted
with a good substantial box thereon, the sides and ends of which shall be not
less than twenty four inches (24") long, so tightly fitted and closely covered
with sufficient covering as to prevent the escape of any of the contents or
effluvia therefrom and so as to prevent such garbage or rubbish to be
scattered, thrown from or dropped onto or upon such street, alley, highway or
thoroughfare. (Ord. 156, 7-7-1950)
8-2-6: DISCARDING GARBAGE, RUBBISH:
It shall be unlawful for any person to distribute, hand out, drop, throw, cast
or discard any wastepaper, paper wrappings, sacks, cartons, boxes, discarded
wrapping paper, garbage or rubbish in, upon or about any street, alley,
sidewalk, avenue or public place, or in or upon any motor vehicle, or in open
spaces, or vacant lots, or in yards or stoops of privately owned premises in
the city; provided, however, it shall not be unlawful to distribute newspapers
capable of being entered in the mail as second class mail. (Ord. 197, 12-21-
1962)
8-2-7: SWEEPING DEBRIS INTO STREETS, FREE ACCESS TO ALLEYS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to sweep dirt, trash or rubbish from the
interior of any building in the city. It shall be unlawful for any person to
park cars or trucks or place any obstruction in alleys. Free access to all
alleys must be had for fire protection and garbage collection at all times.
(Ord. 197, 12-21-1962)
8-2-8: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
The city council shall have the power to make such further rules or
regulations, including the designation of districts for pick up schedules, as
may be necessary to effectuate and facilitate the provisions hereof. (Ord. 197,
12-21-1962)
8-2-9: GARBAGE CONTAINERS REQUIRED; SPECIFICATIONS, PLACEMENT:
   (A)   Containers: The occupant or person in charge of each building,
residence or business housed in the city shall procure and keep on his
premises, when needed, one or more containers in which papers, trash and
similar materials shall be placed. Such garbage containers shall be constructed
of galvanized sheet metal or durable plastic, with tightfitting covers,
provided with two (2) handles and shall have a minimum capacity of three (3)
gallons each and a maximum capacity of thirty (30) gallons each; or such
garbage container may be a heavy duty garbage bag such as will not tear apart
upon being lifted, which garbage bag shall be properly closed. Said containers
shall not be in excess of fifty (50) pounds in weight when filled and shall be
of such size and structure that they can be reasonably loaded. Such garbage
cans and containers shall be placed and kept on the property of the occupant so
owning the same, except that on the day of the week when such garbage shall be
removed, the same shall be placed in the alley adjacent to the building,
residence or business house to be served. In all other cases, such garbage cans
and/or containers shall be placed on the street side of such building,
residence or business house so that they will be accessible to the contractor
in making collections.
   (B)   Open Outdoor Fires:
      1.   It shall be unlawful to have any open outdoor fires or to burn or
cause to be burned any garbage or trash, whether in containers or otherwise,
within the boundaries of the city limits, except for the following purposes and
upon the following conditions:
         (a)   Open outdoor fires used for the purpose of weed abatement along
fence lines, canal banks and ditch banks.
         (b)   Open outdoor fires used to dispose of tree leaves, yard
trimmings and tree limbs.
         (c)   Any other exceptions allowed by fire code.
         (d)   In any event no fires shall be allowed to burn past sunset or
prior to sunrise on any given day.
   (C)   Penalty: Any person who violates any of the provisions of this section
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punishable by a fine of not less than one
hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than three hundred dollars ($300.00). (Ord.
470, 4-5-2007)
8-2-10: GARBAGE SERVICE RATES:
Every occupant or person in charge of any residence, building or business
house, whether such occupant be owner or tenant, shall pay for said service
such sums per month per water meter as may, from time to time, be fixed by
resolution of the city council. For convenience and as a matter of economy in
operation, bills for said service shall be submitted with the bills for service
charges of water and sewer and all three (3) of said service charges shall be
paid as a unit 1 . (Ord. 313, 8-14-1980)
 
Notes
1 1. See sections
  7-3-11 and 7-4-5 of this code, sewer and water charges respectively.
8-2-11: WATER SHUT OFF FOR NONPAYMENT:
In the event any person fails, neglects or refuses to pay said three (3)
service charges or any one thereof, so billed as a unit, within thirty (30)
days of the mailing of such bills by the city, then the city may shut off and
discontinue service to such person for water, sewer and garbage collection, or
any one thereof. In that event such service shall remain disconnected and shut
off until such service charges are paid in full. (Ord. 197, 12-21-1962)
8-2-12: CIVIL ACTION TO COLLECT:
As an additional and concurrent method of enforcing and collecting said garbage
service charge, the city is hereby authorized and empowered to institute civil
action in the appropriate court for the collection of said charge as a civil
debt or obligation. (Ord. 197, 12-21-1962)
CHAPTER 3
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE HABITATION
SECTION:
8-3-1: Purpose
8-3-2: Definitions
8-3-3: Violations
8-3-4: Exceptions
8-3-5: Penalties
8-3-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to limit the use of recreational vehicles and
other nonpermanent structures for permanent human habitation because it is the
determination of the city council that their use in the city for permanent
human habitation is deleterious to the health, safety, and welfare not only of
the persons residing therein, but, additionally, of the public at large.
Portable heating devices, nonstandard electrical connections, a lack of
approved sanitary facilities, including, but not limited to, bathrooms with
toilets, sinks or showers or bathtubs and standard kitchen facilities, among
other facilities associated with safe places of permanent human habitation, all
lend themselves to unhealthful, unsanitary and hazardous living conditions, if
utilized for extended periods of time, occasioned in part because camper
vehicles and other nonpermanent structures are not intended for use as places
of permanent human habitation and do not adequately provide for the needs
associated with human habitation. (Ord. 518-2013, 1-17-2013)
8-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
OCCUPY: The use of a camper vehicle for living, sleeping, dwelling,
housekeeping, business, residence, or other purposes associated with human
occupation or habitation, for any duration and whether or not occurring on an
overnight basis.
OWNER: Any person whose name appears on the public records of the city of
Wendell and county of Gooding, Idaho, as the owner of premises, whether under
deed, contract, bill of sale, or other means of conveyance.
PERSON: Natural person, partnerships, associations, and all other bodies,
corporate or public.
PREMISES: Any lot or parcel of land or real property of any nature, whether
improved or unimproved, including any building or portion thereof.
RV PARK: Any premises within the city of Wendell which has been permitted as a
tract of land designed, maintained or intended for the purpose of supplying
sites for the location of camper vehicles and conforming to all zoning and
building codes and all codified requirements of the city of Wendell.
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE:
Aircraft: A general term applying to all manner of aircraft, whether impelled
by wind or mechanical devices, and which are designed for recreational or
vacation use. An aircraft when mounted upon a trailer shall be considered one
unit.
Camper: A separate vehicle designed for temporary human habitation and which
can be attached or detached from a pickup truck. When removed from the truck,
campers are called "unmounted campers". These campers are sometimes referred to
as "truck campers" and "overhead campers". Camper shells on pickup trucks are
excluded from this definition.
Camper Vehicle: Shall include all campers, camping trailers, motor homes and
travel trailers.
Camping Trailer: A type of trailer or trailer coach, the walls of which are so
constructed as to be collapsible and made out of either canvas or similar
cloth, or some form of rigid material such as fiberglass, plastic or metal. The
walls are collapsed while recreational vehicle is being towed or stored and are
raised or unfolded when the vehicle becomes temporary living quarters and is
not being towed.
Motor Home: A motorized vehicle that has a truck or motor van chassis primarily
designed to provide temporary living quarters for travel, camping, recreation
and vacation use.
Travel Trailer: A trailer without its own motive power, designed as a temporary
dwelling for travel, camping, recreation and vacation use. This definition
includes fifth wheelers.
Utility Trailer: A trailer without its own motive power designed and/or used
for the transportation of animals, goods, material, aircraft, watercraft and
all manner of motor vehicles.
Watercraft: A general term applying to all manner of watercraft, whether
impelled by wind, oars, or mechanical devices, and which are designed primarily
for recreation or vacation use. A watercraft when mounted upon a trailer shall
be considered one unit.
WITHIN THE CORPORATE CITY LIMITS OF WENDELL: Includes, but is not limited to,
residential neighborhoods, commercial and industrial areas, construction sites,
and privately owned property of any nature. (Ord. 518-2013, 1-17-2013)
8-3-3: VIOLATIONS:
Recreational vehicles shall not be used for dwelling, living, sleeping, or
business purposes within the city outside an approved RV park and it shall be
unlawful, within the corporate limits of the city, for any person to park or
allow to be parked any camper vehicle on any premises owned by any person,
whether that vehicle is occupied or unoccupied, except as provided in this
chapter. (Ord. 518-2013, 1-17-2013)
8-3-4: EXCEPTIONS:
   (A)   Temporary Guests: Family or friends of residents who come to visit may
temporarily occupy a camper vehicle situated on the resident's property, but
may only do so for a period not exceeding seven (7) continuous days, and shall
not, under any circumstance, exceed a total of twenty eight (28) days in a
single year. Absolutely no hookup will be allowed to the city of Wendell's
sewer system.
   (B)   Storage Purposes: One recreational vehicle (RV) of any size may be
stored:
      1.   Upon city right of way adjoining owner's property under following
regulations:
         (a)   Thirty feet (30') from any roadway intersection.
         (b)   Twenty feet (20') from any crosswalk.
         (c)   Fifteen feet (15') from any fire hydrant.
      2.   Additional recreational vehicles may be parked under the following
conditions:
         (a)   On the home premises of its owner in a driveway, in a side or
rear yard, or on an adjacent vacant lot owned by the owner of the recreational
vehicle if said recreational vehicle is located at least as far from the lot
lines as may be required by applicable zoning regulations.
         (b)   In an accessory private garage building on the owner's premises.
         (c)   On commercial or industrial premises of the owner, subject to
all zoning restrictions. No camper vehicle so stored or situated outside an RV
park shall be used or occupied for living, sleeping or business purposes.
   (C)   Previously Permitted: Camper vehicles that are located on private
property and which have heretofore been connected with the city water supply
and sanitary sewer system, under a permit granted by the city council or the
building inspector, are excepted from the provisions of this chapter for a
period of six (6) months from the effective date hereof. Such permits may be
extended for no more than a total time of eighteen (18) months. At the
expiration of such time full compliance shall be required.
   (D)   Camper Vehicles On Construction Sites: Occupied camper vehicles will
be allowed on construction sites, subject to the following provisions:
      1.   Permits shall be applied for, and issued by Wendell City Hall
personnel and shall be renewable at the end of each six (6) month period (180
days) for a total period of no longer than eighteen (18) months.
      2.   Each permit must provide a site plan (section
5-14-2 of this code) including: a) make and model of the camper vehicle, b)
license plate identification, c) legal description of the property on which the
camper vehicle is to be located, d) name(s) and mailing address(es) and other
appropriate information.
      3.   Electrical permit issued by the state of Idaho, electrical bureau,
division of public safety must be presented to the city of Wendell prior to a
permit being issued allowing camper vehicle(s) on construction sites.
      4.   Paying a per camper vehicle permit fee and fire inspection fee as
set by city of Wendell fee and rate resolution, payable at the issuance of each
permit and at the time of renewal.
      5.   Obtaining and retaining sewer and water hookups for each permitted
camper vehicle under the terms provided for elsewhere in this code and
inspected by Wendell public works department.
      6.   Only construction workers may occupy permitted camper vehicles.
      7.   Sites must be kept clean of trash and litter.
      8.   Units may be ordered to be removed if legitimate written complaints
are received by the city of Wendell. If units are not removed upon such request
the city may have them removed, with costs assessed against the responsible
parties listed on the permit or, failing that, the property on which such
offending units were located.
      9.   Upon final removal of any such permitted camper vehicle the
responsible parties listed on the permit shall be responsible for capping all
city services and shall be inspected by the Wendell public works department.
(Ord. 518-2013, 1-17-2013)
8-3-5: PENALTIES:
   (A)   Warning: Violations of this chapter set forth under the terms of
section
8-3-3 of this chapter, unless excepted under the terms of the exceptions set
forth in section
8-3-4 of this chapter, shall result in the issuance by the city of Wendell
police department of a warning directed to the owner of the parcel of real
estate upon which said recreational vehicle is situated, informing that person
or persons of the need to cease and desist from allowing such use of the camper
vehicle or other nonpermanent structure for human habitation purposes.
   (B)   Fine: Any person who violates, disobeys, neglects, omits, tries
wilfully to circumvent the intent of this chapter, refuses to comply with this
chapter, or resists enforcement of any of its provisions more than fifteen (15)
days after having received a warning of such violation shall be subject to a
Wendell city ordinance violation fine in the amount of one hundred dollars
($100.00). Failure to cure an issued code and ordinance violation citation
within a time period of ten (10) days may result in additional fines and/or
penalties as provided herein.
   (C)   Additional Remedies: Instead of, or in addition to, the penalties or
relief provided above, the city of Wendell may take such other available legal
action as is necessary to prevent or remedy any violation of this chapter. A
civil action may be commenced and pursued in the Gooding County court for the
purpose of preventing, abating, enjoining, restraining, stopping, or correcting
any violation of this chapter, including, but not limited to, an order
enjoining or preventing the siting and/or occupancy of a camper vehicle in
violation of this chapter. (Ord. 518-2013, 1-17-2013)
TITLE 9
FIRE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
9-1-1: Department Established, Members
9-1-2: Appointment Of Fire Chief, Assistant Fire Chief, Fire Captains, Fire
Marshal; Duties
9-1-3: Oath Of Office
9-1-4: Inspection By Department
9-1-5: Department Equipment
9-1-6: Removal Of Combustible Materials
9-1-7: Police Subject To Fire Call
9-1-8: Fire Drills
9-1-9: Report To Council
9-1-10: Entering Limits Near Fire
9-1-11: Interference With Apparatus At Fire
9-1-12: Permission To Use Fire Apparatus
9-1-13: Obstructing Fire Hydrants
9-1-14: Driving Over Fire Hose
9-1-15: Drivers, Approach Of Fire Vehicles
9-1-1: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED, MEMBERS:
   (A)   There is hereby organized and established a volunteer fire department
for the city to be known as the fire department of the city of Wendell, Idaho.
   (B)   The number of active members of the fire department shall be not more
than thirty (30), nor less than ten (10), all of whom shall be over the age of
eighteen (18) years, and shall be a person of good physique, free from disease
and of good moral character; provided, that no more than twenty (20) of such
members obligated to pay domestic water bills to the city shall be admitted as
members of such department. (1977 Code)
9-1-2: APPOINTMENT OF FIRE CHIEF, ASSISTANT FIRE CHIEF, FIRE CAPTAINS, FIRE
MARSHAL; DUTIES:
The fire chief, assistant fire chief and fire marshal shall be appointed by the
city council, and shall hold office until the expiration of the term of the
appointing power, unless sooner removed by the city council.
The fire captains shall be appointed in the manner as provided in the bylaws of
the fire department, and shall hold office during the pleasure of the fire
chief.
   (A)   Duties Of Chief: The fire chief shall have absolute control of the
fire department at all times, shall call meetings of the members and shall
direct or cause to be directed all improvements of the department and shall see
to it that they keep the apparatus and machinery under their care in proper
order and ready at all times for active duty, and shall supervise and direct
said department in fighting fires, or prevention of fires, and do all things
required to be done to safeguard the city against loss by fire.
   (B)   Duties Of Assistant Chief: It shall be the duty of the assistant fire
chief to attend any fire with the fire chief and assist him in the performance
of his duties, and in the absence of the fire chief, he shall perform the
duties of that office.
   (C)   Duties Of Fire Captains: It shall be the duty of the fire captains to
attend any fire with the fire chief and/or assistant fire chief and assist them
in the performance of their duties and in the absence of the fire chief and the
assistant fire chief, to perform the duties of those offices.
   (D)   Duties Of Fire Marshal: It shall be the duty of the fire marshal to
enforce all of the provisions of this code pertaining to fires and to perform
all fire inspections required by the provisions of this code, ordinances of the
county of Gooding, and statutes of the state of Idaho, and including the
building code, the life safety code (NFP 101) and fire code.
   (E)   Police Powers: When on active duty, the fire chief and assistant fire
chief shall each be vested with the authority of police officers of the city,
with authority to make arrests, and shall each likewise have such police
authority for the purpose of enforcing any ordinance of the city relating to
matters from the duties of that office. (Ord. 120, 3-1937; amd. 1977 Code)
9-1-3: OATH OF OFFICE:
Before entering upon the duties of their offices, the fire chief, assistant
fire chief, fire captains and fire marshal shall take and subscribe an oath to
support the constitution and laws of the state and the ordinances of the city,
and to faithfully perform the duties of their respective offices according to
the best of their ability. (Ord. 120, 3-1937; amd. 1977 Code)
9-1-4: INSPECTION BY DEPARTMENT:
It shall be the duty of the fire chief or fire marshal to inspect or cause to
be inspected by the fire department, its officers or members, as often as may
be necessary, but not less than twice a year in the outlying districts, and
four (4) times a year in closely built portions of the city, all buildings,
premises and public thoroughfares, except the interior of private dwellings,
for the purposes of ascertaining any conditions liable to cause fire, or any
violations of regulations promulgated by the city, for the purpose of reducing
fire hazards. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-5: DEPARTMENT EQUIPMENT:
The equipment of the fire department shall consist of the hose, motorized
equipment and the apparatus now owned by the city, and such additional
equipment as may hereafter be purchased by the city or acquired by the fire
department, together with the fire station and equipment in the nature of
fireplugs and fire hydrants. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-6: REMOVAL OF COMBUSTIBLE MATERIALS:
It shall be the duty of the fire chief, the fire marshal and any police officer
of the city who shall find in any building or upon any premises any combustible
or explosive matter, dangerous accumulations, rubbish, wastepaper, boxes,
shavings, unnecessary accumulations or other inflammable material especially
liable to fire, to order and require the removal of such objectionable material
without delay. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-7: POLICE SUBJECT TO FIRE CALL:
The chief of police, night police and other police officials shall be subject
to duty and call at all fires and said police shall respond and assist in every
way they can in getting the apparatus to the fire and shall take charge and
protect any property needing their protection, and shall keep back the people
from getting in the way, or in any way interfering with the firefighters in the
discharge of their duties, and each of the said police officers shall be under
the orders of the fire chief during a fire. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-8: FIRE DRILLS:
The officers and members of the fire department shall hold fire drills at such
regular intervals as may be prescribed by resolution of the city council from
time to time, and for attending such drills and serving on such fire
department, they shall receive such compensation and be paid at such regular
intervals as may be prescribed by resolution of the city council from time to
time. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-9: REPORT TO COUNCIL:
It shall be the duty of the fire chief and fire marshal to submit complete
reports to the city council at least once each year, and at such other times as
the city council shall demand, showing dates and places of all fires since the
preceding report, the extent of losses suffered, and making recommendations
considered advisable to prevent future losses by fire. The fire chief and fire
marshal shall also report all delinquencies of any member of such department in
the performance of his duty. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-10: ENTERING LIMITS NEAR FIRE:
Whenever a fire shall occur in the city, the fire chief or acting fire chief is
hereby empowered, during the continuance of such fire, to prescribe the limits
within which it shall be unlawful for any persons to come, excepting members of
the fire department, the owners of the premises included in such limits, and
such other persons as may be specially admitted by the fire chief or the acting
fire chief. And it shall be unlawful for any persons other than those above
specified to enter within such limits at any time during the progress of a
fire. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-11: INTERFERENCE WITH APPARATUS AT FIRE:
It shall be unlawful for any person other than the members of the fire
department or police officers, without permission of the fire chief or acting
fire chief, to knowingly or wilfully handle, stand upon or otherwise interfere
with any fire apparatus while the same is being used to extinguish any fire in
the city, or to approach nearer than five hundred feet (500') to the building
on fire. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-12: PERMISSION TO USE FIRE APPARATUS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, unless specially permitted so to do by the
fire chief, assistant fire chief, fire marshal or fire captain, to remove any
fire apparatus, equipment, tools or accessories from the place where same are
kept or to interfere with any fire hydrant, either by turning the water on or
off or attaching any hose, pipe or other connections thereto, or interfering
therewith in any manner whatsoever. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-13: OBSTRUCTING FIRE HYDRANTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person in any manner to obstruct the view of any
fire hydrant or place any material or vehicle in front thereof or within
fifteen feet (15') of either side thereof. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-14: DRIVING OVER FIRE HOSE:
It shall be unlawful for the owner, driver or operator of any engine, motor car
or other vehicle to drive, haul or propel same on or across any of the hose
belonging to the city or the fire department, or to drive or leave such engine,
motor car or other vehicle on any street in such manner as to interfere with or
obstruct any of the fire apparatus or the workings thereof at a fire when an
alarm has been struck. (Ord. 120, 3-1937)
9-1-15: DRIVERS, APPROACH OF FIRE VEHICLES:
The driver of any vehicle within the city, upon the sounding of the fire alarm,
shall immediately stop said vehicle as near as practicable to the right hand
curb, and remain standing until the fire apparatus has passed. (Ord. 120, 3-
1937; amd. 1977 Code)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE LIMITS, REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-2-1: Fire Limits Established
9-2-2: Remodeling, Alteration Of Buildings In Fire Limits
9-2-3: Building Permit Required
9-2-4: Moving Lumber, Buildings
9-2-5: Storing Combustible Materials
9-2-6: Penalty
9-2-1: FIRE LIMITS ESTABLISHED:
The fire limits, of the city shall be that portion of the city defined,
determined and fixed as commercial and industrial zones pursuant to title 5 of
this code. (1977 Code)
   Beginning at the Northeast corner of Block 77;
   Thence west to the Northwest corner of Block 76;
   Thence south to the Southwest corner of Block 105;
   Thence east to the Southeast corner of Lot 18, Block 104;
   Thence north to the Southeast corner of Lot 21, Block 84;
   Thence east to the Southeast corner of Block 84;
   Thence north to the Northeast corner of Block 77, the point of beginning.
(Ord. 251, 4-12-1973)
9-2-2: REMODELING, ALTERATION OF BUILDINGS IN FIRE LIMITS:
No wooden or other building or structure not conforming to the requirements of
the building code of the city and already within the fire limits of the city
shall be remodeled, enlarged, altered, repaired, constructed or reconstructed
with combustible materials in such manner as to increase its height, size or
dimensions; provided, that ordinary deterioration and wear may be repaired, and
also that the building inspector may grant permission to lathe and plaster,
insulate or repair wooden and nonconforming buildings or structures with
noncombustible materials. If any wooden or nonconforming building or structure
within the fire limits suffers damage by fire, wind or other similar elements
to the extent of fifty percent (50%) of the then value of such building or
structure, then the same may not be repaired, rebuilt or reconstructed with any
type of material or under any circumstances, and the owner of such damaged
building or structure shall remove such remnants and debris, and the owner of
such property will be liable to the city for the reasonable costs of such
removal, and the city may file a lien against the land upon which said building
or structure was located. (Ord. 162, 8-14-1953; amd. 1977 Code)
9-2-3: BUILDING PERMIT REQUIRED:
No building or structure shall be constructed, built, remodeled, repaired,
altered or enlarged in the fire limits of the city without a written permit
first had and obtained from the fire marshal. Before such permit is issued,
plans and specifications therefor shall be submitted to and approved by the
fire marshal. Such plans and specifications must show and the fire marshal must
find that the proposed work is in conformity with the requirements of the
building codes of the city, and all amendments to and supplements of said
codes. Upon approval by the fire marshal, a permit shall issue and be signed by
the fire marshal, attested by the city clerk and bear the city seal, and such
permit shall be authority for the person to whom it is issued to proceed with
the work outlined in said plans and specifications. (Ord. 162, 8-14-1953; amd.
1977 Code)
9-2-4: MOVING LUMBER, BUILDINGS:
No lumber or frame buildings within the fire limits of the city shall be
removed to any other part of the fire limits, or from without the fire limits
into said fire limits. (Ord. 12, 4-20-1910)
9-2-5: STORING COMBUSTIBLE MATERIALS:
No person shall, within said fire limits, keep any hay, straw, shavings, paper
or other like combustible material in a stack or pile, without having same
enclosed so as to protect it from flying sparks or fire. (Ord. 12, 4-20-1910)
9-2-6: PENALTY:
Whoever shall, in person or by another, erect any building which may be erected
within the fire limits of the city in violation of any of the provisions of the
building codes shall be liable to a fine as set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code, and if he shall permit the same to remain after receiving
ten (10) days' notice from the chief of police, fire chief or fire marshal to
remove same, he shall be liable to a fine of twenty five dollars ($25.00) for
each day the same shall remain. (Ord. 12, 4-20-1910; amd. 1977 Code)
TITLE 10
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
10-1-1: Assault And Battery
10-1-2: Concealed Weapons
10-1-3: Discharging Firearms, Air Guns
10-1-4: Disturbing Lawful Assemblages
10-1-5: Disturbing The Peace
10-1-6: Fighting
10-1-7: Fraudulently Avoiding Payment Of Admission Fees
10-1-8: Gambling
10-1-9: House Of Prostitution
10-1-10: Indecent Acts, Language
10-1-11: Injuring Property
10-1-12: Liquor Consumption In Public Places
10-1-13: Solicitors, Peddlers, Hawkers, Itinerant Merchants And Transient
Vendors
10-1-13-1: Definitions
10-1-13-2: License Required
10-1-13-3: Applications
10-1-13-4: Investigation And Issuance; Contents Of License
10-1-13-5: Service Of Process
10-1-13-6: Bond
10-1-13-7: License Nontransferable
10-1-13-8: Expiration Of License
10-1-13-9: License Fees
10-1-13-10: Letting Of Private Property Restricted
10-1-13-11: Prohibited Acts
10-1-13-12: Right To Cancel Purchases
10-1-13-13: Appeal
10-1-13-14: Penalty
10-1-14: Playing Ball In Streets
10-1-15: Cigarettes Or Tobacco, Sale Of To Minors
10-1-16: Excessive Noise
10-1-1: ASSAULT AND BATTERY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit an assault and battery within the
limits of the city. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-2: CONCEALED WEAPONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person not a peace officer to carry any slingshot,
brass knuckles, revolver, knife, stiletto or other concealed or deadly weapon,
unless the same be carried on the person in a conspicuous place or in plain
view, within the limits of the city. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-3: DISCHARGING FIREARMS, AIR GUNS:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person not a peace officer in the
discharge of his duties to discharge any gun, revolver or pistol within the
limits of the city, except in the necessary defense of person or property.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person, in any manner, to use devices or
weapons commonly known as air guns, slingshots or flippers on the streets or
the sidewalks of the city. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-4: DISTURBING LAWFUL ASSEMBLAGES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to excite a disturbance or contention at a
public house, court, election or any lawful meeting of citizens or any person
to disturb a public assembly congregated for religious or other lawful purposes
within the limits of the city, by undue noises, or by any offensive, unbecoming
or indecent behavior. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-5: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit a disturbance of the peace within
the limits of the city, by loud or unusual noise, noisy acclamation, offensive,
indecent or obscene language, tumultuous or offensive conduct, or by
threatening, quarreling, challenging to fight or fighting. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-6: FIGHTING:
It shall be unlawful for two (2) or more persons to engage in a fight within
the limits of the city. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-7: FRAUDULENTLY AVOIDING PAYMENT OF ADMISSION FEES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to fraudulently enter any theater,
ballroom, lecture, concert or other place where admission fees are charged
without having first paid said admission fees or with intent to deprive the
owner or proprietor thereof of such fees. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910; amd. 1977 Code)
10-1-8: GAMBLING:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to deal, play or carry on, open or
cause to be opened, or to conduct either as owner, employee or lessee, whether
for hire or not, any games of faro, Monte, roulette, lasquenet, rouge et noir,
rudeo or slot machines for chance, or any games played with cards, dice or any
other device, or money, bank checks, chips, credit or any other representative
of value, within the limits of the city.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly permit any of the
games prohibited in subsection (A) of this section, to be played, conducted or
dealt in any house or room owned or rented by such person in whole or in part.
(Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-9: HOUSE OF PROSTITUTION:
It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to keep a bawdy house, house of
ill fame, or house kept for the purpose of prostitution, within the corporate
limits of the city. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-10: INDECENT ACTS, LANGUAGE:
   (A)   Profanity: It shall be unlawful for any person to abuse another by
using insulting, slanderous or profane language within the limits of the city.
   (B)   Nudity, Indecent Exposure: It shall be unlawful for any person within
the limits of the city to appear in any public place, street, alley or park in
a state of nudity or in any indecent or lewd dress, or to make any indecent
exposures of his or her person, or exhibit or perform any indecent, immoral or
lewd action, or be guilty of any lewd or lascivious conduct. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-11: INJURING PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully injure, deface or destroy any
goods, chattels or valuable papers of another, or prepare any deadfall or dig
any pits or to arrange any trap to injure another person or property, to take
down, injure or remove any monument, street sign or any marks as a boundary of
any tract of land or city lots, or to destroy, deface or alter the marks of any
monuments or street signs or injure or destroy any fence, monument or street
signs or any shade or fruit trees, or any other kind of public property or
private property not belonging to himself, or to deface any sidewalks with
painted or printed handbills or signs, posters or other advertisements, within
the incorporated limits of the city. (Ord. 9, 2-4-1910)
10-1-12: LIQUOR CONSUMPTION IN PUBLIC PLACES:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to consume or cause to be consumed
any beer or intoxicating liquor in any public place or building or at any
public gathering, within the limits of the city. Provided, however, that this
shall not apply to premises which hold a current and valid license to dispense
beer or intoxicating liquor or an event granted a catering permit, which may be
issued by the city pursuant to Idaho Code section 23-934A for consumption of
alcoholic beverages at the city park. A catering permit will only be granted in
conjunction with the granting of a completed special event application as may
be required by the City Council which shall be attached to a catering permit
application. A catering permit requires City Council approval, fourteen (14)
days prior to the event. "Public place", as defined in this section, includes
any place, building or conveyance, to which the public has or is permitted to
have access, and any place, highway, street, lane, park or place of public
resort or amusement, within the limits of the city.
   (B)   Any person violating any of the provisions of this section shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in any sum not less than twenty five dollars
($25.00) nor more than three hundred dollars ($300.00), or imprisonment in the
city jail for a period not to exceed thirty (30) days, or by both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 228, 9-24-1970; amd. Ord. 538-2021, 7-15-2021)
10-1-13: SOLICITORS, PEDDLERS, HAWKERS, ITINERANT MERCHANTS AND TRANSIENT
VENDORS:
10-1-13-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter:
 
           Any person, whether a resident of the city or not, traveling by foot, motor
           vehicle or any other type of conveyance, however propelled, drawn, pushed or
           moved, from place to place, from house to house or from street to street,
           carrying, conveying or transporting goods, wares, merchandise, food or farm
PEDDLER:   products or provisions, offering and exposing the same for sale or making sales
           and delivering articles to purchasers, or who, without traveling from place to
           place shall sell or offer the same for sale from a wagon, vehicle, railroad car,
           or any other type of conveyance. The word "peddler" shall include the words
           "hauler" and "hucksters".
           Any person, whether a resident of the city or not, traveling either by foot,
           motor vehicle or any other type of conveyance, from place to place, from house to
           house or from street to street, taking or attempting to take, in person, orders
           for sale of goods, wares and merchandise, personal property of any nature
SOLICITOR  whatsoever for future delivery, or for services to be furnished or performed in
OR         the future, whether he is collecting advance payments on such sales or not. Such
CANVASSER: definitions shall include any person who, for himself, or for another person
           hires, leases, uses or occupies any building, structure, tent, railroad boxcar,
           boat, hotel room, lodging house, apartment, shop or any other place within the
           city for the sole purpose of exhibiting samples and taking orders for future
           delivery.
           Any person, firm or corporation, whether as owner, agent, consignee, or employee,
           whether a resident of the city or not, who engages in a temporary business of
           selling and delivering goods, wares and merchandise within the city and who, in
           furtherance of such purpose, hires, leases, uses or occupies any public or
           private place, building, motor vehicle, tent, railroad boxcar, public room in a
           hotel, lodging house, apartment, shop or any street or other place within the
           city for the exhibition and sale of such goods, wares and merchandise, either
           privately or at public auction.
           A "temporary business" is one which is expected to be in operation for six (6)
           months or less within the city. This definition shall not include nor be
           construed to include:
           (A)   Public or private auction for the disposal by an established business of
           its assets or an individual for items of personal and household use.
           (B)   Any person, partnership or corporation selling or dealing only with retail
           merchants within the city, and being exclusively wholesale sellers and dealers.
           (C)   Any religious or charitable corporation or organization engaging in any one
           or more of the above activities for strictly nonprofit purposes.
TRANSIENT  (D)   Any arts or crafts shows or fairs where the items for sale are exhibited by
MERCHANT,  the person producing the items; and, the exhibitor was invited by the sponsoring
ITINERANT  party; the names of participants are accumulated by the sponsoring party to be
MERCHANT   made available to the city council or clerk.
OR         (E)   Any sales pursuant to court order.
ITINERANT  (F)   The sale of farm or garden products by the persons producing such products.
VENDOR:    (G)   The sale of a newspaper subscription in which the seller is a person
           engaged in both the delivery and sale of the newspaper.
           (H)   Political groups seeking funds or memberships.
           (I)   Sales of Christmas trees and wreaths.
           The person, partnership or corporation so engaged shall not be relieved from
           complying with the provisions of this chapter merely by reason of associating
           temporarily with any local dealer, trader, merchant or auctioneer, or by
           conducting such transient business in connection with, as a part of or in the
           name of any local dealer, trader, merchant or auctioneer.
           Any person, partnership or corporation wishing to engage in any one or more of
           the activities described above, and not specifically excluded from the definition
           of the itinerant merchant, peddler, or solicitor as set forth above, may petition
           the city council and upon good cause shown, the city council may exempt the
           person, partnership or corporation from application of this chapter.
           Notwithstanding the foregoing, any person or business intending to conduct
           business continuously for at least one year in the city, or having conducted
           business in the city continuously for the previous year, and can provide proof by
           way of a written lease, contract or other proof satisfactory to the city clerk,
           shall be exempt from the application of this chapter. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
 
10-1-13-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for a transient merchant, itinerant merchant, itinerant
vendor, peddler or solicitor, as defined in section
10-1-13-1 of this chapter, to engage in such business within the city without
first obtaining a license therefor in compliance with the provisions of this
chapter. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-3: APPLICATIONS:
Applications for licenses by solicitors and peddlers shall be made to the city
clerk, to his designee or to the chief of police or other applicable law
enforcement agency, and shall be sworn in writing and shall contain the
following information:
   (A)   Name of applicant;
   (B)   Permanent address of applicant;
   (C)   Temporary address of applicant, if any;
   (D)   Idaho state sales tax license number and, if applicable, Idaho
corporation license number;
   (E)   A brief description of the nature of the business to be conducted and
the goods to be sold, and if the goods are farm or orchard products, a
statement as to the point of origin for the product;
   (F)   If the products are imported into the state from an area outside the
state, the person receiving the application may require a certificate that the
product is disease free, insect free, properly fumigated and will in no way
spread any disease, fungi, bacteria, insect or animal illnesses or diseases of
any kind;
   (G)   A statement as to whether the applicant is self-employed or working
for an employer;
   (H)   If the applicant is selling goods for another, a statement as to who
the owners of the goods are;
   (I)   A two inch by two-inch (2" x 2") photograph showing the head and
shoulders in a clear and distinguishable manner of the applicant and the person
selling, delivering, conveying, carrying, transporting goods, wares,
merchandise, food or like merchandise of the applicant or offering to perform
services in the present or future for applicant;
   (J)   A statement that in the event that the product causes any damage to
any resident of the city, the applicant acknowledges the jurisdiction of the
Idaho courts to resolve any disputes;
   (K)   The length of time for which the license requested shall be needed;
   (L)   A description of the vehicle to be used in the solicitation, peddling
or vending, together with the license number thereof;
   (M)   A statement as to whether or not the applicant or applicant's employer
has been convicted of any crime in violation of any consumer protection laws or
of any peddlers' or solicitors' ordinances. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-4: INVESTIGATION AND ISSUANCE; CONTENTS OF LICENSE:
   (A)   Investigation And Issuance: Upon receipt of the application, the chief
of police or other applicable law enforcement agency shall cause such
investigation of the applicant's business responsibility or moral character to
be made. The chief of police or other applicable law enforcement agency may
utilize such departments of the city, county or state as deemed appropriate in
the aid of the investigation. When the chief of police or other applicable law
enforcement agency requests a criminal history record check by the criminal
identification bureau of the department of law enforcement, State of Idaho, the
chief of police or other applicable law enforcement agency shall forward the
applicant's fingerprints to the criminal identification bureau for a statewide
criminal history check. As a result of the investigation, if the applicant's
character and business responsibility are found to be unsatisfactory, the
application shall be denied. If, as a result of the investigation, the
character and business reputation appear to be satisfactory, the city clerk
shall so certify in writing and a license shall be issued if all of the
requirements of this chapter have been met.
   (B)   Record: The city clerk shall keep a full record in his or her office
of all licenses issued, and each such license shall contain the number of the
license, the date the same was issued, the nature of the business authorized to
be carried on, the amount of the license fee paid, the expiration date of the
license, and the place where such business may be carried on under said
license, the name or names of the person or persons authorized to carry on the
same. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-5: SERVICE OF PROCESS:
Before any license herein provided for shall be issued for engaging in the
business of an itinerant merchant, as herein defined, such applicant shall file
with the city clerk an instrument nominating and appointing the city clerk his
true and lawful agent with full power and authority to acknowledge service of
notice of process for and on behalf of said applicant in respect to any matters
connected with or arising out of the business transacted under said license,
which said instrument shall also contain recitals to the effect that said
applicant for said license consents and agrees that service of any notice or
process may be made upon said agent. Said instrument shall also contain
recitals to the effect that said applicant for said license consents and agrees
that service of any notice or process may be made upon said agent, and when so
made shall be taken and held to be as valid as if personally served upon the
person or persons applying for the license under this chapter, according to the
law of this or any other state, and waiving any claim or right of error by
reason of such acknowledgment of service or manner of service. Immediately upon
service or process upon the city clerk, as herein provided, the city clerk
shall send to the licensee at his last known address, by registered mail, a
copy of said process. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-6: BOND:
Before any license, as provided by this chapter shall be issued for engaging in
a transient or itinerant business as defined in this chapter in the city, such
applicant shall file with the city clerk a bond running to the city in the sum
of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) executed by the applicant, as principal,
and two (2) sureties upon which service of process may be made in the state of
Idaho; said bond to be approved by the city attorney, conditioned that the said
applicant shall comply fully with all the provisions of the ordinances of the
city and the statutes of the state of Idaho regulating and concerning the sale
of goods, wares and merchandise, and will pay all judgments rendered against
said applicant for any violation of said laws or statutes, or any of them
together with all judgments and costs that may be recovered against him by any
person or persons for damage growing out of any misrepresentation or deception
practiced on any person or persons transacting such business with such
applicant, whether said misrepresentations or deceptions were made or practiced
by the owners or by their servants, agents, or employees, either at the time of
making the sale or through any advertisement of any character whatsoever,
printed, or circulated with reference to the goods, wares and merchandise sold
or any part thereof. Action on the bond may be brought in the name of the city
to the use of the aggrieved person. Such bond must be approved by the city
attorney, both as to form and as to the responsibility of the sureties thereon.
(Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-7: LICENSE NONTRANSFERABLE:
No license issued or granted by the city shall in any manner be assignable or
transferable or authorize any person other than the one therein named to do
business or authorize any other business than is therein mentioned to be done
or authorize the transaction of such business at any other place than is
specified in the license. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-8: EXPIRATION OF LICENSE:
All licenses issued under the provisions of this chapter shall expire ninety
(90) days after the date of issuance thereof unless a prior date is fixed
therein. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-9: LICENSE FEES:
A license will be issued for a specified period and in accordance with the fee
schedule hereinafter enacted, as the same may be changed from time to time by
resolution of the city council. Payment for the licenses shall be made upon
filing of the application with the proper authority and shall be made in lawful
currency of the United States.
The city shall collect license fees in the amounts set forth below:
Auctioneers holding regular auctions at a specified location $100.00 per year
within the city limits
Circuses and carnivals                                       200.00 per day
Itinerant merchants, peddlers, agents, independent           15.00 per day
contractors, hawkers, hucksters, solicitors
Selling from motor vehicles, pickups, trailers, trucks or    25.00 per day
wagons
Sideshows or performances, whether human, animal or nonhuman 25.00 per day
Street stands                                                25.00 per day
Transient auctioneers or auctioneers holding nonrecurring    15.00 per day
sales
All other businesses not specified in this code              100.00 per year
 
By accepting a fee and issuing a license, the city does not assume any
liability for any actions or any conduct engaged in by the licensee. The city,
nor any of its employees, shall endorse any products or services sold by any
licensees and the city, employees of the city and any licensees shall not
represent to any person that the city has any interest in any business carried
on by the licensee. (Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-10: LETTING OF PRIVATE PROPERTY RESTRICTED:
No property owner, nor his agent or employee, shall sublet, lease, sublease or
otherwise permit his property, or property of which he is in charge, to be used
by an itinerant merchant or itinerant vendor, as herein defined, unless
specifically excluded from application of this chapter or unless the itinerant
vendor or itinerant merchant has obtained a license as provided herein. (Ord.
542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-11: PROHIBITED ACTS:
A licensee, or any person acting on behalf of a licensee, or any agent of a
licensee, shall not:
   (A)   Shout, make an outcry, blow a horn, ring a bell or use any sound
device or musical instrument, including any loud speaking radio or sound
amplifying system, on any of the streets, alleys, parks, or other public places
of the city, or on any private premises within the city, where sound of
sufficient volume is emitted or produced therefrom, to be capable of being
plainly heard on the streets, avenues, alleys, parks or other public places for
the purpose of attracting attention to any goods, wares, or merchandise which
such licensee proposes to sell.
   (B)   Have any mechanical devices in human or animal form or otherwise
designed to create lights, sound or motion to attract passersby.
   (C)   Have any exclusive right to any location in the public streets, shall
not be permitted a stationary location and shall not be permitted to operate in
any congested area where licensee's operations might impede or inconvenience
the public. For purposes of enforcement of this chapter, the judgment of any
police officer, exercised in good faith, shall be deemed conclusive as to
whether or not an area is congested or the public is impeded or inconvenienced
by the presence of the licensee.
   (D)   Sell or offer for sale goods, wares, or merchandise from vehicles on
any of the public streets of the city. Licensees shall not be allowed to double
park or in any way impede the normal flow of traffic or create a hazard or a
nuisance upon any public roadway.
   (E)   Be allowed to solicit or peddle from sundown to nine o'clock (9:00)
A.M., or at any time when a sign has been clearly posted on a fence, driveway,
front, back or side yard, or doorway which clearly informs a licensee that
there shall be no solicitors or no peddlers, either using those words or in
words to that effect. Providing, however, that a licensee may call upon the
occupant of a residence at other times when he has expressed prior permission
from such occupant to do so.
   (F)   Make any representation that he or she is soliciting or peddling for
any nonprofit organization or for charitable or religious purposes if he or she
in any way shall personally benefit by the funds or properties solicited.
   (G)   Cast, throw, distribute, deposit, scatter, pass out, give away,
circulate or deliver any commercial or business handbills, dodgers, circulars,
or other advertising materials or devices to any residents or businesses, or
leave the same upon any porch, doorstep, entryway, vestibule or in any yard or
public hallway, or in any vacant lot or upon other private property in the
city, without first having obtained the expressed consent of the owner or
lessee, or without the written or expressed request of any adult resident or
occupant thereof.
   (H)   Make any false statement or claims as to the quality, value, origin,
condition, durability, or purpose as to any product.
   (I)   Make false representations as to any product which he is soliciting
for or peddling.
   (J)   No licensee shall distribute, sell, or hand out as a sample any
consumable food products which have not been properly approved by the state
health district, the South Central Public Health District, the federal trade
commission or any other state or federal agency which has jurisdiction as to
the quality or wholesomeness of any foodstuffs designed for human consumption.
(Ord. 542-2021, - -)
10-1-13-12: RIGHT TO CANCEL PURCHASES:
Any person purchasing from any solicitor or peddler or salesman pursuant to any
home solicitation shall have three (3) business days from the day of sale to
cancel any sale or any security or any contract created during the consummation
of the sale. Any licensee, salesman, solicitor, or peddler shall have an
affirmative duty to inform any purchaser of that person's right of
cancellation. In the event of cancellation, the purchaser must make the product
available to the seller at the purchaser's residence in as good a condition as
the product was when it was received for a period of twenty (20) days after the
notice of cancellation. If the salesman does not retrieve the product within
twenty (20) days from the date of notice of cancellation, the purchaser may
